     </a>\n         </sup>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">\n         Website\n        </th>\n        <td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n         <span class="url">\n          <a class="external text" href="http://bbc.co.uk" rel="nofollow">\n           bbc\n           <wbr/>\n           .co\n           <wbr/>\n           .uk\n          </a>\n         </span>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <b>\n        British Broadcasting Corporation\n       </b>\n       (\n       <b>\n        BBC\n       </b>\n       ) is a British\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_service_broadcaster" title="Public service broadcaster">\n        public service broadcaster\n       </a>\n       with its headquarters at\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">\n        Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">\n        London\n       </a>\n       . The BBC is the world\'s oldest national broadcasting organisation\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historicalbroadcaster_4-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-historicalbroadcaster-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the largest\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting" title="Broadcasting">\n        broadcaster\n       </a>\n       in the world by number of employees. It employs over 20,950 staff in total, 16,672 of whom are in public sector broadcasting.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013-14-c1-persons-employed_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2013-14-c1-persons-employed-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MediaNewsline_6-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-MediaNewsline-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProspectMag_7-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-ProspectMag-7">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AboutBBC_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-AboutBBC-8">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Annual_Report_9-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Annual_Report-9">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The total number of staff is 35,402 when part-time, flexible, and fixed contract staff are included.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC is established under a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Charter#United_Kingdom" title="Royal Charter">\n        Royal Charter\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crown_11-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-crown-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and operates under its Agreement with the Secretary of State for Culture, Media and Sport.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Its work is funded principally by an annual\n       <a href="/wiki/Television_licensing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Television licensing in the United Kingdom">\n        television licence fee\n       </a>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrustAR_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TrustAR-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which is charged to all British households, companies, and organisations using any type of equipment to receive or record live\n       <a href="/wiki/Television" title="Television">\n        television\n       </a>\n       broadcasts and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">\n        iPlayer\n       </a>\n       catch-up.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TVLic_14-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TVLic-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The fee is set by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Government of the United Kingdom">\n        British Government\n       </a>\n       , agreed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">\n        Parliament\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TVLic2_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TVLic2-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and used to fund the BBC\'s radio, TV, and online services covering the nations and regions of the UK. Since 1 April 2014, it has also funded the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n        BBC World Service\n       </a>\n       (launched in 1932 as the BBC Empire Service), which broadcasts in 28 languages and provides comprehensive TV, radio, and online services in\n       <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">\n        Arabic\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">\n        Persian\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Around a quarter of BBC revenues come from its commercial arm\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Worldwide" title="BBC Worldwide">\n        BBC Worldwide Ltd\n       </a>\n       , which sells BBC programmes and services internationally and also distributes the BBC\'s international 24-hour English-language news services\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">\n        BBC World News\n       </a>\n       , and from BBC.com, provided by BBC Global News Ltd.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#History">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           1\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           History\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-2">\n           <a href="#The_birth_of_British_broadcasting.2C_1920_to_1922">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             The birth of British broadcasting, 1920 to 1922\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3">\n           <a href="#From_private_company_towards_public_service_corporation.2C_1923_to_1926">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             From private company towards public service corporation, 1923 to 1926\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4">\n           <a href="#1927_to_1939">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             1927 to 1939\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5">\n           <a href="#BBC_versus_other_media">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             BBC versus other media\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-6">\n           <a href="#1939_to_2001">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.5\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             1939 to 2001\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-7">\n           <a href="#2000_to_2011">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2000 to 2011\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8">\n           <a href="#2011_to_present">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             1.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             2011 to present\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9">\n         <a href="#Governance_and_corporate_structure">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           2\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Governance and corporate structure\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10">\n           <a href="#Charter">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Charter\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">\n           <a href="#BBC_Board">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             BBC Board\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12">\n </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13">\n           <a href="#Operational_divisions">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             2.4\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Operational divisions\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14">\n   </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19">\n         <a href="#Technology_.28Atos_service.29">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           5\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Technology (Atos service)\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20">\n         <a              6.1.1\n              </span>\n              <span class="toctext">\n               Genome Project\n              </span>\n             </a>\n            </li>\n           </ul>\n  6.3\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             News\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25">\n           <a   </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26">\n           <a href="#Interactive_television">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.5\n            </span>\n            <span <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.6\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Music\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-28">\n           <a href="#Other">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.7\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Other\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29">\n           <a href="#Ceefax">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             6.8\n streaming service\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-31">\n         <a href="#Commercial_activities">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           7\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Commercial activities\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-32">\n         <a href="#Cultural_significance">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           8\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Cultural significance\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33">\n           <a href="#Attitudes_toward_the_BBC_in_popular_culture">\n       </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-34">\n         <a href="#Criticism_and_controversies">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           9\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           Criticism and controversies\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-35">\n         <a  <span class="tocnumber">\n           12\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           See also\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-38">\n         <a href="#References">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           13\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           References\n          </span>\n         </a>\n         <ul>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-39">\n           <a href="#Citations">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             13.1\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Citations\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40">\n           <a href="#Sources">\n            <span class="tocnumber">\n             13.2\n            </span>\n            <span class="toctext">\n             Sources\n            </span>\n           </a>\n          </li>\n         </ul>\n        </li>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-41">\n         <a href="#External_links">\n          <span class="tocnumber">\n           14\n          </span>\n          <span class="toctext">\n           External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">\n        History\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_BBC" title="Timeline of the BBC">\n        Timeline of the BBC\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="The_birth_of_British_broadcasting,_1920_to_1922">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_birth_of_British_broadcasting.2C_1920_to_1922">\n        The birth of British broadcasting, 1920 to 1922\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The birth of British broadcasting, 1920 to 1922">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Britain\'s first live public broadcast from the Marconi factory in Chelmsford took place in June 1920. It was sponsored by the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Daily_Mail" title="Daily Mail">\n         Daily Mail\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\n        \'\n       </span>\n       s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Northcliffe" title="Lord Northcliffe">\n        Lord Northcliffe\n       </a>\n       and featured the famous Australian soprano\n       <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Melba" title="Nellie Melba">\n        Dame Nellie Melba\n       </a>\n       . The Melba broadcast caught the people\'s imagination and marked a turning point in the British public\'s attitude to radio.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, this public enthusiasm was not shared in official circles where such broadcasts were held to interfere with important military and civil communications. By late 1920, pressure from these quarters and uneasiness among the staff of the licensing authority, the\n       <a href="/wiki/General_Post_Office" title="General Post Office">\n        General Post Office\n       </a>\n       (GPO), was sufficient to lead to a ban on further Chelmsford broadcasts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       But by 1922, the GPO had received nearly 100 broadcast licence requests\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and moved to rescind its ban in the wake of a petition by 63 wireless societies with over 3,000 members.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Anxious to avoid the same chaotic expansion experienced in the United States the GPO proposed that it would issue a single broadcasting licence to a company jointly owned by a consortium of leading wireless receiver manufactures, to be known as the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Broadcasting_Company" title="British Broadcasting Company">\n        British Broadcasting Company Ltd.\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Reith,_1st_Baron_Reith" title="John Reith, 1st Baron Reith">\n        John Reith\n       </a>\n       , a Scottish Calvinist, was appointed its General Manager in December 1922 a few weeks after the company made its first official broadcast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The company was to be financed by a royalty on the sale of BBC wireless receiving sets from approved manufacturers. To this day, the BBC aims to follow the Reithian directive to "inform, educate and entertain".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [21]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="From_private_company_towards_public_service_corporation,_1923_to_1926">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="From_private_company_towards_public_service_corporation.2C_1923_to_1926">\n        From private company towards public service corporation, 1923 to 1926\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: From private company towards public service corporation, 1923 to 1926">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The financial arrangements soon proved inadequate. Set sales were disappointing as amateurs made their own receivers and listeners bought rival unlicensed sets.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [22]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       By mid-1923, discussions between the GPO and the BBC had become deadlocked and the Postmaster-General commissioned a review of broadcasting by the\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sykes_Committee&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sykes Committee (page does not exist)">\n        Sykes Committee\n       </a>\n       . The Committee recommended a short term reorganisation of licence fees with improved enforcement in order to address the BBC\'s immediate financial distress, and an increased share of the licence revenue split between it and the GPO. This was to be followed by a simple 10 shillings licence fee with no royalty once the wireless manufactures protection expired. The BBC\'s broadcasting monopoly was made explicit for the duration of its current broadcast licence, as was the prohibition on advertising. The BBC was also banned from presenting news bulletins before 19.00, and required to source all news from external wire services.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Mid-1925 found the future of broadcasting under further consideration, this time by the Crawford committee. By now the BBC under Reith\'s leadership had forged a consensus favouring a continuation of the unified (monopoly) broadcasting service, but more money was still required to finance rapid expansion. Wireless manufacturers were anxious to exit the loss making consortium with Reith keen that the BBC be seen as a public service rather than a commercial enterprise. The recommendations of the Crawford Committee were published in March the following year and were still under consideration by the GPO when the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1926_general_strike" title="1926 general strike">\n        1926 general strike\n       </a>\n       broke out in May. The strike temporarily interrupted newspaper production and with restrictions on news bulletins waived the BBC suddenly became the primary source of news for the duration of the crisis.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supra_Curran_and_Seaton.2C_p._117_23-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-supra_Curran_and_Seaton.2C_p._117-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The crisis placed the BBC in a delicate position. On one hand Reith was acutely aware that the Government might exercise its right to commandeer the BBC at any time as a mouthpiece of the Government if the BBC were to step out of line, but on the other he was anxious to maintain public trust by appearing to be acting independently. The Government was divided on how to handle the BBC but ended up trusting Reith, whose opposition to the strike mirrored the PM\'s own. Thus the BBC was granted sufficient leeway to pursue the Government\'s objectives largely in a manner of its own choosing. The resulting coverage of both striker and government viewpoints impressed millions of listeners who were unaware that the PM had broadcast to the nation from Reith\'s home, using one of Reith\'s sound bites inserted at the last moment, or that the BBC had banned broadcasts from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">\n        Labour Party\n       </a>\n       and delayed a peace appeal by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">\n        Archbishop of Canterbury\n       </a>\n       . Supporters of the strike nicknamed the BBC the BFC for British Falsehood Company. Reith personally announced the end of the strike which he marked by reciting from Blake\'s "\n       <a href="/wiki/And_did_those_feet_in_ancient_time" title="And did those feet in ancient time">\n        Jerusalem\n       </a>\n       " signifying that England had been saved.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n        <a href="#cite_note-24">\n         [24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       While the BBC tends to characterise its coverage of the general strike by emphasising the positive impression created by its balanced coverage of the views of government and strikers, Jean Seaton, Professor of Media History and the Official BBC Historian has characterised the episode as the invention of "modern propaganda in its British form".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supra_Curran_and_Seaton.2C_p._117_23-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-supra_Curran_and_Seaton.2C_p._117-23">\n         [23]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Reith argued that trust gained by \'authentic impartial news\' could then be used. Impartial news was not necessarily an end in itself.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">\n        <a href="#cite_note-25">\n         [25]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC did well out of the crisis, which cemented a national audience for its broadcasting, and it was followed by the Government\'s acceptance of the recommendation made by the Crawford Committee (1925\xe2\x80\x9326) that the British Broadcasting Company be replaced by a non-commercial, Crown-chartered organisation: the British Broadcasting Corporation.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="1927_to_1939">\n        1927 to 1939\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1927 to 1939">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5397" data-file-width="3918" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg/220px-John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg/330px-John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg/440px-John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:John_Logie_Baird_in_1917.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Television pioneer\n         <a href="/wiki/John_Logie_Baird" title="John Logie Baird">\n          John Logie Baird\n         </a>\n         televised the BBC\'s first drama,\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/The_Man_with_the_Flower_in_His_Mouth" title="The Man with the Flower in His Mouth">\n           The Man with the Flower in His Mouth\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         , on 14 July 1930, and the first live outside broadcast,\n         <a href="/wiki/Epsom_Derby" title="Epsom Derby">\n          The Derby\n         </a>\n         , on 2 June 1931.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">\n          <a href="#cite_note-26">\n           [26]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">\n          <a href="#cite_note-27">\n           [27]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The British Broadcasting Corporation came into existence on 1 January 1927, and Reith \xe2\x80\x93 newly knighted \xe2\x80\x93 was appointed its first Director General. To represent its purpose and (stated) values, the new corporation adopted the\n       <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_the_BBC" title="Coat of arms of the BBC">\n        coat of arms\n       </a>\n       , including the motto "Nation shall speak peace unto Nation".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Motto_28-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Motto-28">\n         [28]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       British radio audiences had little choice apart from the upscale programming of the BBC. Reith, an intensely moralistic executive, was in full charge. His goal was to broadcast "All that is best in every department of human knowledge, endeavour and achievement.... The preservation of a high moral tone is obviously of paramount importance."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">\n        <a href="#cite_note-29">\n         [29]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Reith succeeded in building a high wall against an American-style free-for-all in radio in which the goal was to attract the largest audiences and thereby secure the greatest advertising revenue. There was no paid advertising on the BBC; all the revenue came from a tax on receiving sets. Highbrow audiences, however, greatly enjoyed it.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">\n        <a href="#cite_note-30">\n         [30]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       At a time when American, Australian and Canadian stations were drawing huge audiences cheering for their local teams with the broadcast of baseball, rugby and hockey, the BBC emphasized service for a national, rather than a regional audience. Boat races were well covered along with tennis and horse racing, but the BBC was reluctant to spend its severely limited air time on long football or cricket games, regardless of their popularity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">\n        <a href="#cite_note-31">\n         [31]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="BBC_versus_other_media">\n        BBC versus other media\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: BBC versus other media">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_broadcast,_Christmas_1934_(Our_Generation,_1938).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="1806" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Royal_broadcast%2C_Christmas_1934_%28Our_Generation%2C_1938%29.jpg/220px-Royal_broadcast%2C_Christmas_1934_%28Our_Generation%2C_1938%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Royal_broadcast%2C_Christmas_1934_%28Our_Generation%2C_1938%29.jpg/330px-Royal_broadcast%2C_Christmas_1934_%28Our_Generation%2C_1938%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Royal_broadcast%2C_Christmas_1934_%28Our_Generation%2C_1938%29.jpg/440px-Royal_broadcast%2C_Christmas_1934_%28Our_Generation%2C_1938%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_broadcast,_Christmas_1934_(Our_Generation,_1938).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">\n          George V\n         </a>\n         giving the 1934\n         <a href="/wiki/Royal_Christmas_Message" title="Royal Christmas Message">\n          Royal Christmas Message\n         </a>\n         on BBC Radio. The annual message typically chronicles the year\'s major events.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The success of broadcasting provoked animosities between the BBC and well established media such as theatres, concert halls and the recording industry. By 1929, the BBC complained that the agents of many comedians refused to sign contracts for broadcasting, because they feared it harmed the artist "by making his material stale" and that it "reduces the value of the artist as a visible music-hall performer". On the other hand, the BBC was "keenly interested" in a cooperation with the recording companies who "in recent years\xc2\xa0... have not been slow to make records of singers, orchestras, dance bands, etc. who have already proved their power to achieve popularity by wireless." Radio plays were so popular that the BBC had received 6,000 manuscripts by 1929, most of them written for stage and of little value for broadcasting: "Day in and day out, manuscripts come in, and nearly all go out again through the post, with a note saying \'We regret, etc.\'"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">\n        <a href="#cite_note-32">\n         [32]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the 1930s music broadcasts also enjoyed great popularity, for example the friendly and wide-ranging organ broadcasts at St George\'s Hall, Langham Place, by\n       <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Foort" title="Reginald Foort">\n        Reginald Foort\n       </a>\n       , who held the official role of BBC Staff Theatre Organist from 1936 to 1938; Foort continued to work for the BBC as a freelance into the 1940s and enjoyed a nationwide following.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Experimental television broadcasts were started in 1930, using an electromechanical 30-line system developed by\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Logie_Baird" title="John Logie Baird">\n        John Logie Baird\n       </a>\n       . Limited regular broadcasts using this system began in 1934, and an expanded service (now named the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television#History_of_BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">\n        BBC Television Service\n       </a>\n       ) started from\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Palace" title="Alexandra Palace">\n        Alexandra Palace\n       </a>\n       in 1936, alternating between an improved Baird mechanical 240 line system and the all electronic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/405_line" title="405 line">\n        405 line\n       </a>\n       Marconi-EMI system. The superiority of the electronic system saw the mechanical system dropped early the following year.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">\n        <a href="#cite_note-33">\n         [33]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="1939_to_2001">\n        1939 to 2001\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1939 to 2001">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Television broadcasting was suspended from 1 September 1939 to 7 June 1946, during the\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        Second World War\n       </a>\n       , and it was left to\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">\n        BBC Radio\n       </a>\n       broadcasters such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Reginald_Foort" title="Reginald Foort">\n        Reginald Foort\n       </a>\n       to keep the nation\'s spirits up. The BBC moved much of its radio operations out of London, initially to Bristol, and then to Bedford. Concerts were broadcast from the Corn Exchange; the Trinity Chapel in\n       <a href="/wiki/St_Paul%27s_Church,_Bedford" title="St Paul\'s Church, Bedford">\n        St Paul\'s Church, Bedford\n       </a>\n       was the studio for the daily service from 1941 to 1945 and, in the darkest days of the war in 1941, the Archbishops of Canterbury and York came to St Paul\'s to broadcast to the UK and all parts of the world on the National Day of Prayer.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       There was a widely reported urban myth that, upon resumption of the BBC television service after the war, announcer\n       <a href="/wiki/Leslie_Mitchell_(broadcaster)" title="Leslie Mitchell (broadcaster)">\n        Leslie Mitchell\n       </a>\n       started by saying, "As I was saying before we were so rudely interrupted\xc2\xa0..." In fact, the first person to appear when transmission resumed was\n       <a href="/wiki/Jasmine_Bligh" title="Jasmine Bligh">\n        Jasmine Bligh\n       </a>\n       and the words said were "Good afternoon, everybody. How are you? Do you remember me, Jasmine Bligh\xc2\xa0...\xc2\xa0?"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">\n        <a href="#cite_note-34">\n         [34]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Broadcasting_Union" title="European Broadcasting Union">\n        European Broadcasting Union\n       </a>\n       was formed on 12 February 1950, in\n       <a href="/wiki/Torquay" title="Torquay">\n        Torquay\n       </a>\n       with the BBC among the 23 founding broadcasting organisations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">\n        <a href="#cite_note-35">\n         [35]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_TV_Centre.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/BBC_TV_Centre.jpg/220px-BBC_TV_Centre.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/BBC_TV_Centre.jpg/330px-BBC_TV_Centre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/BBC_TV_Centre.jpg/440px-BBC_TV_Centre.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_TV_Centre.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n          BBC Television Centre\n         </a>\n         at\n         <a href="/wiki/White_City,_London" title="White City, London">\n          White City\n         </a>\n         , West London, which opened in 1960 and closed in 2013.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Competition to the BBC was introduced in 1955, with the commercial and independently operated television network of\n       <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">\n        ITV\n       </a>\n       . However, the BBC monopoly on radio services would persist until 8 October 1973 when under the control of the newly renamed\n       <a href="/wiki/Independent_Broadcasting_Authority" title="Independent Broadcasting Authority">\n        Independent Broadcasting Authority\n       </a>\n       (IBA) the UK\'s first Independent local radio station,\n       <a href="/wiki/LBC" title="LBC">\n        LBC\n       </a>\n       came on-air in the London area. As a result of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Pilkington_Committee_on_Broadcasting" title="Pilkington Committee on Broadcasting">\n        Pilkington Committee\n       </a>\n       report of 1962, in which the BBC was praised for the quality and range of its output, and ITV was very heavily criticised for not providing enough quality programming,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">\n        <a href="#cite_note-36">\n         [36]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the decision was taken to award the BBC a second television channel,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">\n        BBC2\n       </a>\n       , in 1964, renaming the existing service\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC1" title="BBC1">\n        BBC1\n       </a>\n       . BBC2 used the higher resolution 625 line standard which had been standardised across Europe. BBC2 was broadcast in colour from 1 July 1967, and was joined by BBC1 and ITV on 15 November 1969. The 405 line\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vhf#United_Kingdom" title="Vhf">\n        VHF\n       </a>\n       transmissions of BBC1 (and ITV) were continued for compatibility with older television receivers until 1985.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Starting in 1964, a series of\n       <a href="/wiki/Pirate_radio" title="Pirate radio">\n        pirate radio\n       </a>\n       stations (starting with\n       <a href="/wiki/Radio_Caroline" title="Radio Caroline">\n        Radio Caroline\n       </a>\n       ) came on the air and forced the British government finally to regulate radio services to permit nationally based advertising-financed services. In response, the BBC reorganised and renamed their radio channels. On 30 September 1967, the Light Programme was split into\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">\n        Radio 1\n       </a>\n       offering continuous "Popular" music and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">\n        Radio 2\n       </a>\n       more "Easy Listening".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">\n        <a href="#cite_note-37">\n         [37]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The "Third" programme became\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3" title="BBC Radio 3">\n        Radio 3\n       </a>\n       offering classical music and cultural programming. The Home Service became\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">\n        Radio 4\n       </a>\n       offering news, and non-musical content such as quiz shows, readings, dramas and plays. As well as the four national channels, a series of local BBC radio stations were established in 1967, including\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_London_94.9" title="BBC London 94.9">\n        Radio London\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">\n        <a href="#cite_note-38">\n         [38]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1969, the BBC Enterprises department was formed to exploit BBC brands and programmes for commercial\n       <a href="/wiki/Spin-off_(media)" title="Spin-off (media)">\n        spin-off\n       </a>\n       products. In 1979, it became a wholly owned limited company, BBC Enterprises Ltd.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-briggs_39-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-briggs-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1974, the BBC\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Teletext" title="Teletext">\n        teletext\n       </a>\n       service,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ceefax" title="Ceefax">\n        Ceefax\n       </a>\n       , was introduced, created initially to provide subtitling, but developed into a news and information service. In 1978, BBC staff went on strike just before the Christmas of that year, thus blocking out the transmission of both channels and amalgamating all four radio stations into one.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">\n        <a href="#cite_note-40">\n         [40]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">\n        <a href="#cite_note-41">\n         [41]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since the deregulation of the UK television and radio market in the 1980s, the BBC has faced increased competition from the commercial sector (and from the advertiser-funded public service broadcaster\n       <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">\n        Channel 4\n       </a>\n       ), especially on satellite television, cable television, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">\n        digital television\n       </a>\n       services.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the late 1980s, the BBC began a process of\n       <a href="/wiki/Divestment" title="Divestment">\n        divestment\n       </a>\n       by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spin_out" title="Spin out">\n        spinning off\n       </a>\n       and selling parts of its organisation. In 1988, it sold off the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hulton_Press_Library" title="Hulton Press Library">\n        Hulton Press Library\n       </a>\n       , a photographic archive which had been acquired from the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Picture_Post" title="Picture Post">\n         Picture Post\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       magazine by the BBC in 1957. The archive was sold to\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Brian_Deutsch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Brian Deutsch (page does not exist)">\n        Brian Deutsch\n       </a>\n       and is now owned by\n       <a href="/wiki/Getty_Images" title="Getty Images">\n        Getty Images\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hulton-history_42-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-hulton-history-42">\n         [42]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       During the 1990s, this process continued with the separation of certain operational arms of the corporation into autonomous but\n       <a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">\n        wholly owned subsidiaries\n       </a>\n       of the BBC, with the aim of generating additional revenue for programme-making. BBC Enterprises was reorganised and relaunched in 1995, as BBC Worldwide Ltd.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-briggs_39-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-briggs-39">\n         [39]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 1998, BBC studios, outside broadcasts, post production, design, costumes and wigs were spun off into BBC Resources Ltd.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian-resources_43-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-guardian-resources-43">\n         [43]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Research_Department" title="BBC Research Department">\n        BBC Research Department\n       </a>\n       has played a major part in the development of broadcasting and recording techniques. In the early days, it carried out essential research into acoustics and programme level and noise measurement.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2007)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       The BBC was also responsible for the development of the\n       <a href="/wiki/NICAM" title="NICAM">\n        NICAM\n       </a>\n       stereo standard.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In recent decades, a number of additional channels and radio stations have been launched:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_(former)" title="BBC Radio 5 (former)">\n        Radio 5\n       </a>\n       was launched in 1990, as a sports and educational station, but was replaced in 1994, with\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">\n        Radio 5 Live\n       </a>\n       , following the success of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_News_FM" title="BBC Radio 4 News FM">\n        Radio 4 service\n       </a>\n       to cover the 1991 Gulf War. The new station would be a news and sport station. In 1997,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_News_24" title="BBC News 24">\n        BBC News 24\n       </a>\n       , a rolling news channel, launched on\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">\n        digital television\n       </a>\n       services and the following year,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Choice" title="BBC Choice">\n        BBC Choice\n       </a>\n       launched as the third general entertainment channel from the BBC. The BBC also purchased The Parliamentary Channel, which was renamed\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Parliament" title="BBC Parliament">\n        BBC Parliament\n       </a>\n       . In 1999,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Knowledge" title="BBC Knowledge">\n        BBC Knowledge\n       </a>\n       launched as a multi media channel, with services available on the newly launched\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Red_Button" title="BBC Red Button">\n        BBC Text\n       </a>\n       digital teletext service, and on\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">\n        BBC Online\n       </a>\n       . The channel had an educational aim, which was modified later on in its life to offer documentaries.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2000_to_2011">\n        2000 to 2011\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000 to 2011">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In 2002, several television and radio channels were reorganised.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Knowledge" title="BBC Knowledge">\n        BBC Knowledge\n       </a>\n       was replaced by\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Four" title="BBC Four">\n        BBC Four\n       </a>\n       and became the BBC\'s arts and documentaries channel.\n       <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">\n        CBBC\n       </a>\n       , which had been a programming strand as Children\'s BBC since 1985, was split into CBBC and\n       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">\n        CBeebies\n       </a>\n       , for younger children, with both new services getting a digital channel: the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CBBC_Channel" title="CBBC Channel">\n        CBBC Channel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">\n        CBeebies\n       </a>\n       Channel. In addition to the television channels, new digital radio stations were created:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1Xtra" title="BBC Radio 1Xtra">\n        1Xtra\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_6_Music" title="BBC Radio 6 Music">\n        6 Music\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_Extra" title="BBC Radio 4 Extra">\n        BBC7\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1Xtra" title="BBC Radio 1Xtra">\n        BBC 1Xtra\n       </a>\n       was a sister station to\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">\n        Radio 1\n       </a>\n       and specialised in modern black music,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_6_Music" title="BBC Radio 6 Music">\n        BBC 6 Music\n       </a>\n       specialised in alternative music genres and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_Extra" title="BBC Radio 4 Extra">\n        BBC7\n       </a>\n       specialised in archive, speech and children\'s programming.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The following few years resulted in repositioning of some of the channels to conform to a larger brand: in 2003,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Choice" title="BBC Choice">\n        BBC Choice\n       </a>\n       was replaced by\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">\n        BBC Three\n       </a>\n       , with programming for younger generations and shocking real life documentaries, BBC News 24 became the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_News_Channel" title="BBC News Channel">\n        BBC News Channel\n       </a>\n       in 2008, and BBC Radio 7 became\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_Extra" title="BBC Radio 4 Extra">\n        BBC Radio 4 Extra\n       </a>\n       in 2011, with new programmes to supplement those broadcast on\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">\n        Radio 4\n       </a>\n       . In 2008, another channel was launched,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Alba" title="BBC Alba">\n        BBC Alba\n       </a>\n       , a\n       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">\n        Scottish Gaelic\n       </a>\n       service.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       During this decade, the corporation began to sell off a number of its operational divisions to private owners; BBC Broadcast was spun off as a separate company in 2002,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-broadcast-ltd_44-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-broadcast-ltd-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and in 2005. it was sold off to\n       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n        Australian\n       </a>\n       -based Macquarie Capital Alliance Group and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macquarie_Bank" title="Macquarie Bank">\n        Macquarie Bank\n       </a>\n       Limited and rebranded\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Bee_Media" title="Red Bee Media">\n        Red Bee Media\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">\n        <a href="#cite_note-45">\n         [45]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The BBC\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">\n        IT\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Telephony" title="Telephony">\n        telephony\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_engineering" title="Broadcast engineering">\n        broadcast technology\n       </a>\n       were brought together as BBC Technology Ltd in 2001,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-broadcast-ltd_44-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-broadcast-ltd-44">\n         [44]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the division was later sold to the German engineering and electronics company\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siemens_IT_Solutions_and_Services" title="Siemens IT Solutions and Services">\n        Siemens IT Solutions and Services\n       </a>\n       (SIS).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-2204_46-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-2204-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       SIS was subsequently acquired from Siemens by the French company\n       <a href="/wiki/Atos" title="Atos">\n        Atos\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atos-ariel_47-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atos-ariel-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Further divestments in this decade included\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Books" title="BBC Books">\n        BBC Books\n       </a>\n       (sold to\n       <a href="/wiki/Random_House" title="Random House">\n        Random House\n       </a>\n       in 2006);\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">\n        <a href="#cite_note-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       BBC Outside Broadcasts Ltd (sold in 2008. to\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Information_Services" title="Satellite Information Services">\n        Satellite Information Services\n       </a>\n       );\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OBsale_49-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-OBsale-49">\n         [49]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Costumes and Wigs (stock sold in 2008 to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angels_The_Costumiers" title="Angels The Costumiers">\n        Angels The Costumiers\n       </a>\n       );\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-angels-costumes_50-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-angels-costumes-50">\n         [50]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Magazines" title="BBC Magazines">\n        BBC Magazines\n       </a>\n       (sold to\n       <a href="/wiki/Immediate_Media_Company" title="Immediate Media Company">\n        Immediate Media Company\n       </a>\n       in 2011).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">\n        <a href="#cite_note-51">\n         [51]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       After the sales of OBs and costumes, the remainder of BBC Resources was reorganised as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Studios_and_Post_Production" title="BBC Studios and Post Production">\n        BBC Studios and Post Production\n       </a>\n       , which continues today as a wholly owned subsidiary of the BBC.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The 2004\n       <a href="/wiki/Hutton_Inquiry" title="Hutton Inquiry">\n        Hutton Inquiry\n       </a>\n       and the subsequent Report raised questions about the BBC\'s journalistic standards and its impartiality. This led to resignations of senior management members at the time including the then Director General,\n       <a href="/wiki/Greg_Dyke" title="Greg Dyke">\n        Greg Dyke\n       </a>\n       . In January 2007, the BBC released minutes of the board meeting which led to Greg Dyke\'s resignation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n        <a href="#cite_note-52">\n         [52]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Unlike the other departments of the BBC, the BBC World Service was funded by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">\n        Foreign and Commonwealth Office\n       </a>\n       . The Foreign and Commonwealth Office, more commonly known as the Foreign Office or the FCO, is the British government department responsible for promoting the interests of the United Kingdom abroad.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Scotland.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/BBC_Scotland.jpg/220px-BBC_Scotland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/BBC_Scotland.jpg/330px-BBC_Scotland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/BBC_Scotland.jpg/440px-BBC_Scotland.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Scotland.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_Pacific_Quay" title="BBC Pacific Quay">\n          BBC Pacific Quay\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">\n          Glasgow\n         </a>\n         , which was opened in 2007.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In 2006,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_HD" title="BBC HD">\n        BBC HD\n       </a>\n       launched as an experimental service, and became official in December 2007. The channel broadcast HD simulcasts of programmes on\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">\n        BBC One\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">\n        BBC Two\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">\n        BBC Three\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Four" title="BBC Four">\n        BBC Four\n       </a>\n       as well as repeats of some older programmes in HD. In 2010, an HD simulcast of BBC One launched:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_One_HD" title="BBC One HD">\n        BBC One HD\n       </a>\n       . The channel uses HD versions of BBC One\'s schedule and uses upscaled versions of programmes not currently produced in HD. The BBC HD channel closed in March 2013 and was replaced by BBC2 HD in the same month.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 18 October 2007, BBC Director General Mark Thompson announced a controversial plan to make major cuts and reduce the size of the BBC as an organisation. The plans included a reduction in posts of 2,500; including 1,800 redundancies, consolidating news operations, reducing programming output by 10% and selling off the flagship\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n        Television Centre\n       </a>\n       building in London.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n        <a href="#cite_note-53">\n         [53]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       These plans have been fiercely opposed by unions, who have threatened a series of strikes; however, the BBC have stated that the cuts are essential to move the organisation forward and concentrate on increasing the quality of programming.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 20 October 2010, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_the_Exchequer" title="Chancellor of the Exchequer">\n        Chancellor of the Exchequer\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/George_Osborne" title="George Osborne">\n        George Osborne\n       </a>\n       announced that the television licence fee would be frozen at its current level until the end of the current charter in 2016. The same announcement revealed that the BBC would take on the full cost of running the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n        BBC World Service\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Monitoring" title="BBC Monitoring">\n        BBC Monitoring\n       </a>\n       service from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">\n        Foreign and Commonwealth Office\n       </a>\n       , and partially finance the Welsh broadcaster\n       <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">\n        S4C\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n        <a href="#cite_note-54">\n         [54]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="2011_to_present">\n        2011 to present\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2011 to present">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="733" data-file-width="679" height="237" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG/220px-BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG/330px-BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG/440px-BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBCBroadcastingHouse.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         BBC New Broadcasting House, London which came into use during 2012\xe2\x80\x9313\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Further cuts were announced on 6 October 2011, so the BBC could reach a total reduction in their budget of 20%, following the licence fee freeze in October 2010, which included cutting staff by 2,000 and sending a further 1,000 to the\n       <a href="/wiki/MediaCityUK" title="MediaCityUK">\n        MediaCityUK\n       </a>\n       development in\n       <a href="/wiki/Salford,_Greater_Manchester" title="Salford, Greater Manchester">\n        Salford\n       </a>\n       , with BBC Three moving online only in 2016, the sharing of more programmes between stations and channels, sharing of radio news bulletins, more repeats in schedules, including the whole of BBC Two daytime and for some original programming to be reduced.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_HD" title="BBC HD">\n        BBC HD\n       </a>\n       was closed on 26 March 2013, and replaced with an HD simulcast of BBC Two; however, flagship programmes, other channels and full funding for\n       <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">\n        CBBC\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">\n        CBeebies\n       </a>\n       would be retained.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">\n        <a href="#cite_note-55">\n         [55]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n        <a href="#cite_note-56">\n         [56]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n        <a href="#cite_note-57">\n         [57]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Numerous BBC facilities have been sold off, including\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Broadcasting_House_(Manchester)" title="New Broadcasting House (Manchester)">\n        New Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_Road,_Manchester" title="Oxford Road, Manchester">\n        Oxford Road\n       </a>\n       in Manchester. Many major departments have been relocated to\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">\n        Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/MediaCityUK" title="MediaCityUK">\n        MediaCityUK\n       </a>\n       , particularly since the closure of BBC Television Centre in March 2013.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">\n           citation needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       On 16 February 2016, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">\n        BBC Three\n       </a>\n       television service was discontinued and replaced by an\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three_(online)" title="BBC Three (online)">\n        digital outlet\n       </a>\n       under the same name, targeting its young adult audience with web series and other content.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">\n        <a href="#cite_note-58">\n         [58]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n        <a href="#cite_note-59">\n         [59]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n        <a href="#cite_note-60">\n         [60]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under the new royal charter instituted 2017, the corporation must publish an annual report to Ofcom, outlining its plans and public service obligations for the next year. In its 2017\xe2\x80\x9318 report, released July 2017, the BBC announced plans to "re-invent" its output to better compete against commercial streaming services such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Netflix" title="Netflix">\n        Netflix\n       </a>\n       . These plans included increasing the diversity of its content on television and radio, a major increase in investments towards digital children\'s content, and plans to make larger investments in other nations of the United Kingdom besides England to "rise to the challenge of better reflecting and representing a changing UK"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">\n        <a href="#cite_note-61">\n         [61]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n        <a href="#cite_note-62">\n         [62]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_and_corporate_structure">\n        Governance and corporate structure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Governance and corporate structure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The BBC is a statutory corporation, independent from direct government intervention, with its activities being overseen from April 2017 by the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Board" title="BBC Board">\n        BBC Board\n       </a>\n       and regulated by\n       <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">\n        Ofcom\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ofcom_63-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Ofcom-63">\n         [63]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n        <a href="#cite_note-64">\n         [64]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Chairman is Sir\n       <a href="/wiki/David_Clementi" title="David Clementi">\n        David Clementi\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n        <a href="#cite_note-65">\n         [65]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Charter">\n        Charter\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Charter">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The BBC operates under a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Charter#United_Kingdom" title="Royal Charter">\n        Royal Charter\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-crown_11-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-crown-11">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The current Charter came into effect on 1 January 2017 and runs until 31 December 2026.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Royal_Charter_66-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Royal_Charter-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The 2017 charter abolished the BBC Trust and replaced it with external regulation by\n       <a href="/wiki/Ofcom" title="Ofcom">\n        Ofcom\n       </a>\n       , with governance by the BBC Board.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Royal_Charter_66-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Royal_Charter-66">\n         [66]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Under the Royal Charter, the BBC must obtain a licence from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Home_Secretary" title="Home Secretary">\n        Home Secretary\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbchow_67-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbchow-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This licence is accompanied by an agreement which sets the terms and conditions under which the BBC is allowed to broadcast.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbchow_67-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbchow-67">\n         [67]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="BBC_Board">\n        BBC Board\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: BBC Board">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Board" title="BBC Board">\n        BBC Board\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC Board was formed in April 2017. It replaced the previous governing body, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Trust" title="BBC Trust">\n        BBC Trust\n       </a>\n       , which in itself had replaced the\n       <a href="/wiki/Board_of_Governors_of_the_BBC" title="Board of Governors of the BBC">\n        Board of Governors\n       </a>\n       in 2007. The Board sets the strategy for the corporation, assesses the performance of the BBC Executive Board in delivering the BBC\'s services, and appoints the Director-General. Regulation of the BBC is now the responsibility of Ofcom. The Board consists of the following members.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Board_and_Executive_68-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Board_and_Executive-68">\n         [68]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">\n        <a href="#cite_note-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n MacQuarrie\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director, Nations and Regions\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" to 2 April 2013\n           </li>\n           <li>\n            <b>\n             <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hall,_Baron_Hall_of_Birkenhead" title="Tony Hall, Baron Hall of Birkenhead">\n              Tony Hall\n             </a>\n            </b>\n            2 April 2013 \xe2\x80\x93 present\n           </li>\n          </ul>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-text" colspan="2">\n         List of BBC\n         <a href="/wiki/Director-General_of_the_BBC" title="Director-General of the BBC">\n          Directors General\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       The Executive Committee is responsible for the day-to-day operations of the broadcaster. Consisting of senior managers of the BBC, the Committee meets once per month and is responsible for operational management and delivery of services within a framework set by the Board, and is chaired by the Director-General, currently\n       <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hall,_Baron_Hall_of_Birkenhead" title="Tony Hall, Baron Hall of Birkenhead">\n        Tony Hall\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Director-General_of_the_BBC" title="Director-General of the BBC">\n        Director-General\n       </a>\n       is chief executive and (from 1994) editor-in-chief.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n
