     <tr>\n        <td>\n         Charlotte Moore\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director of Content\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Mark Linsey\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director of BBC Studios\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/James_Harding_(journalist)" title="James Harding (journalist)">\n          James Harding\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director of News &amp; Current Affairs\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Postgate" title="Matthew Postgate">\n          Matthew Postgate\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Chief Technology &amp; Research Officer\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ken_MacQuarrie" title="Ken MacQuarrie">\n          Ken MacQuarrie\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director of Nations &amp; Regions\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/James_Purnell" title="James Purnell">\n          James Purnell\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director of Radio &amp; Education\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a href="/wiki/Tim_Davie" title="Tim Davie">\n          Tim Davie\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         CEO, BBC Worldwide\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Valerie_Hughes_D%27Aeth&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Valerie Hughes D\'Aeth (page does not exist)">\n          Valerie Hughes D\'Aeth\n         </a>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Director of HR\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_divisions">\n        Operational divisions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Operational divisions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The Corporation has the following in-house divisions covering the BBC\'s output and operations:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_71-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Content\n        </b>\n        , headed by\n        <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Moore_(TV_executive)" title="Charlotte Moore (TV executive)">\n         Charlotte Moore\n        </a>\n        is in charge of the corporation\'s\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">\n         television channels\n        </a>\n        including the commissioning of programming.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Radio and Education\n        </b>\n        headed by\n        <a href="/wiki/James_Purnell" title="James Purnell">\n         James Purnell\n        </a>\n        is in charge of\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">\n         BBC Radio\n        </a>\n        and music content across the BBC under the\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Music" title="BBC Music">\n         BBC Music\n        </a>\n        brand, including music programmes on BBC Television, events such as the\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Proms" title="BBC Proms">\n         BBC Proms\n        </a>\n        and the numerous\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Orchestras_and_Singers" title="BBC Orchestras and Singers">\n         orchestras\n        </a>\n        such as the\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Philharmonic" title="BBC Philharmonic">\n         BBC Philharmonic\n        </a>\n        , as well as\n        <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">\n         Children\'s BBC\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         News and Current Affairs\n        </b>\n        headed by\n        <a href="/wiki/James_Harding_(journalist)" title="James Harding (journalist)">\n         James Harding\n        </a>\n        operates the\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">\n         BBC News\n        </a>\n        operation, including the national, regional and international output on television, radio and online, as well as the output of the BBC Global News division. It is also in charge of the corporation\'s Current Affairs programming and have some responsibility for\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">\n         sports\n        </a>\n        output.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The\n        <b>\n         Deputy Director General Group\n        </b>\n        headed by\n        <a href="/wiki/Anne_Bulford" title="Anne Bulford">\n         Anne Bulford\n        </a>\n        , contains\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Design_and_Engineering" title="BBC Design and Engineering">\n         Design &amp; Engineering\n        </a>\n        , which is in charge of all digital output, such as\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">\n         BBC Online\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">\n         BBC iPlayer\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Red_Button" title="BBC Red Button">\n         BBC Red Button\n        </a>\n        service and developing new technologies through\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Research_%26_Development" title="BBC Research &amp; Development">\n         BBC Research &amp; Development\n        </a>\n        . The division also includes other pan-BBC functions including Finance, HR, Strategy, Security and Property.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_71-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-71">\n          [71]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Nations and Regions\n        </b>\n        , headed by Ken MacQuarrie is responsible for the Corporation\'s divisions in\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">\n         Scotland\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">\n         Northern Ireland\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Cymru_Wales" title="BBC Cymru Wales">\n         Wales\n        </a>\n        , the\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_English_Regions" title="BBC English Regions">\n         English Regions\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_divisions">\n        Commercial divisions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Commercial divisions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The BBC also operates a number of wholly owned commercial divisions:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_Worldwide" title="BBC Worldwide">\n          BBC Worldwide\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        Ltd, headed by\n        <a href="/wiki/Tim_Davie" title="Tim Davie">\n         Tim Davie\n        </a>\n        , operates international channels and sells programmes and merchandise in the UK and abroad to gain additional income that is returned to BBC programmes. It is kept separate from the corporation due to its commercial nature.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">\n          BBC World News\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        department is in charge of the production and distribution of its commercial global television channel. It works closely with the BBC News group, but is not governed by it, and shares the corporation\'s facilities and staff. It also works with BBC Worldwide, the channel\'s distributor.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_Studios" title="BBC Studios">\n          BBC Studios\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        , headed by\n        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mark_Linsey&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mark Linsey (page does not exist)">\n         Mark Linsey\n        </a>\n        is the former in-house television production; Entertainment, Music &amp; Events, Factual and Scripted (drama and comedy).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_Studioworks" title="BBC Studioworks">\n          BBC Studioworks\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        is also separate and officially owns and operates some of the BBC\'s studio facilities, such as the\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Elstree_Centre" title="BBC Elstree Centre">\n         BBC Elstree Centre\n        </a>\n        , leasing them out to productions from within and outside of the corporation.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_71-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-71">\n          [71]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">\n        Finances\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Finances">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The BBC has the second largest budget of any UK-based broadcaster with an operating expenditure of \xc2\xa34.722\xc2\xa0billion in 2013/14\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013-14-consolidated-income-statement_72-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2013-14-consolidated-income-statement-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       compared to \xc2\xa36.471\xc2\xa0billion for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Sky_Broadcasting" title="British Sky Broadcasting">\n        British Sky Broadcasting\n       </a>\n       in 2013/14\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and \xc2\xa31.843\xc2\xa0billion for\n       <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">\n        ITV\n       </a>\n       in the calendar year 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Revenue">\n        Revenue\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Revenue">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       See also:\n       <a href="/wiki/Television_licence" title="Television licence">\n        Television licence\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Television_licensing_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Television licensing in the United Kingdom">\n        Television licensing in the United Kingdom\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The principal means of funding the BBC is through the television licence, costing \xc2\xa3145.50 per year per household since April 2010. Such a licence is required to legally receive broadcast television across the UK, the Channel Islands and the Isle of Man. No licence is required to own a television used for other means, or for sound only radio sets (though a separate licence for these was also required for non-TV households until 1971). The cost of a television licence is set by the government and enforced by the criminal law. A discount is available for households with only black-and-white television sets. A 50% discount is also offered to people who are registered blind or severely visually impaired,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the licence is completely free for any household containing anyone aged 75 or over. As a result of the UK Government\'s recent spending review, an agreement has been reached between the government and the corporation in which the current licence fee will remain frozen at the current level until the Royal Charter is renewed at the beginning of 2017.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The revenue is collected privately\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2016)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       and is paid into the central government\n       <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_Fund" title="Consolidated Fund">\n        Consolidated Fund\n       </a>\n       , a process defined in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Communications_Act_2003" title="Communications Act 2003">\n        Communications Act 2003\n       </a>\n       . The BBC pursues its licence fee collection and enforcement under the trading name "TV Licensing".\n       <i>\n        TV Licensing\n       </i>\n       collection is currently carried out by Capita, an outside agency. Funds are then allocated by the Department of Culture, Media and Sport (DCMS) and the Treasury and approved by Parliament via legislation. Additional revenues are paid by the Department for Work and Pensions to compensate for subsidised licences for eligible over-75-year-olds.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The licence fee is classified as a tax,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Select_Committee_20060303_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Select_Committee_20060303-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and its evasion is a criminal offence. Since 1991, collection and enforcement of the licence fee has been the responsibility of the BBC in its role as TV Licensing Authority.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KeyFacts_78-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KeyFacts-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Thus, the BBC is a major prosecuting authority in England and Wales and an investigating authority in the UK as a whole. The BBC carries out surveillance (mostly using subcontractors) on properties (under the auspices of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Regulation_of_Investigatory_Powers_Act_2000" title="Regulation of Investigatory Powers Act 2000">\n        Regulation of Investigatory Powers Act 2000\n       </a>\n       ) and may conduct searches of a property using a search warrant.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC25AUG2006_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC25AUG2006-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to the BBC, "more than 204,000 people in the UK were caught watching TV without a licence during the first six months of 2012."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">\n        <a href="#cite_note-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Licence fee evasion makes up around one tenth of all cases prosecuted in magistrates\' courts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prosecutions_81-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-prosecutions-81">\n         [81]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Income from commercial enterprises and from overseas sales of its catalogue of programmes has substantially increased over recent years,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n        <a href="#cite_note-82">\n         [82]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       with\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Worldwide" title="BBC Worldwide">\n        BBC Worldwide\n       </a>\n       contributing some \xc2\xa3145\xc2\xa0million to the BBC\'s core public service business.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       According to the BBC\'s 2013/14 Annual Report, its total income was \xc2\xa35 billion (\xc2\xa35.066 billion),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013-14-a1-income-and-operating-results_2-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2013-14-a1-income-and-operating-results-2">\n         [2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       which can be broken down as follows:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        \xc2\xa33.726 billion in licence fees collected from householders;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        \xc2\xa31.023 billion from the BBC\'s commercial businesses;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        \xc2\xa3244.6\xc2\xa0million from government grants, of which \xc2\xa3238.5\xc2\xa0million is from the\n        <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">\n         Foreign and Commonwealth Office\n        </a>\n        for the\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n         BBC World Service\n        </a>\n        ;\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        \xc2\xa372.1\xc2\xa0million from other income, such as rental collections and royalties from overseas broadcasts of programming.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2013-14-a1-income-and-operating-results_2-2">\n         <a href="#cite_note-2013-14-a1-income-and-operating-results-2">\n          [2]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       The licence fee has, however, attracted criticism. It has been argued that in an age of multi stream, multi-channel availability, an obligation to pay a licence fee is no longer appropriate. The BBC\'s use of private sector company\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Capita_Group" title="Capita Group">\n        Capita Group\n       </a>\n       to send letters to premises not paying the licence fee has been criticised, especially as there have been cases where such letters have been sent to premises which are up to date with their payments, or do not require a TV licence.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">\n        <a href="#cite_note-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC uses advertising campaigns to inform customers of the requirement to pay the licence fee. Past campaigns have been criticised by\n       <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">\n        Conservative\n       </a>\n       MP\n       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Johnson" title="Boris Johnson">\n        Boris Johnson\n       </a>\n       and former MP\n       <a href="/wiki/Ann_Widdecombe" title="Ann Widdecombe">\n        Ann Widdecombe\n       </a>\n       for having a threatening nature and language used to scare evaders into paying.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n        <a href="#cite_note-84">\n         [84]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">\n        <a href="#cite_note-85">\n         [85]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Audio clips and television broadcasts are used to inform listeners of the BBC\'s comprehensive database.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">\n        <a href="#cite_note-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       There are a number of pressure groups campaigning on the issue of the licence fee.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">\n        <a href="#cite_note-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The majority of the BBC\'s commercial output comes from its commercial arm\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Worldwide" title="BBC Worldwide">\n        BBC Worldwide\n       </a>\n       who sell programmes abroad and exploit key brands for merchandise. Of their 2012/13 sales, 27% were centred on the five key "superbrands" of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">\n         Doctor Who\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(2002_TV_series)" title="Top Gear (2002 TV series)">\n         Top Gear\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Strictly_Come_Dancing" title="Strictly Come Dancing">\n         Strictly Come Dancing\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       (known as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars" title="Dancing with the Stars">\n         Dancing with the Stars\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       internationally), the BBC\'s archive of natural history programming (collected under the umbrella of\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Earth" title="BBC Earth">\n        BBC Earth\n       </a>\n       ) and the (now sold) travel guide brand\n       <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Planet" title="Lonely Planet">\n        Lonely Planet\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Worldwide_2012.2F13_review_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Worldwide_2012.2F13_review-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Expenditure">\n        Expenditure\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Expenditure">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The following expenditure figures are from 2012/13\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_annual_report_finance_expenditure_89-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13_annual_report_finance_expenditure-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and show the expenditure of each service they are obliged to provide:\n      </p>\n      <div class="floatright">\n       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Expenditures_2012-2013.png">\n        <img alt="BBC Expenditures 2012-2013.png" data-file-height="520"       </tr>\n       <tr style="background:#ffffe0">\n        <th style="background:#ffffe0">\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_switchover" title="Digital switchover">\n Restructuring\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         23.1\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="background:#e0ffff">\n        <th style="background:#e0ffff">\n         Property\n      175.1\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="background:#ffe0e0">\n        <th style="background:#ffe0e0">\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_Trust" title="BBC Trust">\n          BBC Trust\n         </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         11.9\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="background:#ffffe0">\n        <th style="background:#ffffe0">\n         Libraries, learning support and community events\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         33.6\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="background:#9cf;">\n        <th style="background:#9cf;">\n         Other, including training, marketing, finance and policy\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         925.9\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         <i>\n          Total\n         </i>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           4,896\n          </b>\n         </i>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       A significantly large portion of the BBC\'s income is spent on the corporation\'s Television and Radio services with each service having a different budget based upon their content.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2012.2F13_annual_report_finance_expenditure_89-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-2012.2F13_annual_report_finance_expenditure-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n     </a>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         17.6\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         + 1.7\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr style="background:#ffdead">\n        <th   <th>\n         <i>\n          Total\n         </i>\n        </th>\n        <td>\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           669.5\n          </b>\n         </i>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         + 29.4\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters_and_regional_offices">\n        Headquarters and regional offices\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Headquarters and regional offices">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/List_of_BBC_properties" title="List of BBC properties">\n        List of BBC properties\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">\n        Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House_(Belfast)" title="Broadcasting House (Belfast)">\n        Broadcasting House (Belfast)\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House_(Cardiff)" title="Broadcasting House (Cardiff)">\n        Broadcasting House (Cardiff)\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n        BBC Television Centre\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg/170px-Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg/255px-Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg/340px-Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Broadcasting_House_by_Stephen_Craven.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The headquarters of the BBC at\n         <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">\n          Broadcasting House\n         </a>\n         in\n         <a href="/wiki/Portland_Place" title="Portland Place">\n          Portland Place\n         </a>\n         , London, England. This section of the building is called "Old Broadcasting House".\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House" title="Broadcasting House">\n        Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Portland_Place" title="Portland Place">\n        Portland Place\n       </a>\n       , London, is the official headquarters of the BBC. It is home to six of the ten BBC national radio networks, BBC Radio 1, BBC Radio 1xtra, BBC Asian Network,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3" title="BBC Radio 3">\n        BBC Radio 3\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">\n        BBC Radio 4\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_Extra" title="BBC Radio 4 Extra">\n        BBC Radio 4 Extra\n       </a>\n       . It is also the home of\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">\n        BBC News\n       </a>\n       , which relocated to the building from\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n        BBC Television Centre\n       </a>\n       in 2013. On the front of the building are statues of\n       <a href="/wiki/Prospero" title="Prospero">\n        Prospero\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Ariel_(The_Tempest)" title="Ariel (The Tempest)">\n        Ariel\n       </a>\n       , characters from\n       <a href="/wiki/William_Shakespeare" title="William Shakespeare">\n        William Shakespeare\n       </a>\n       \'s play\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Tempest" title="The Tempest">\n         The Tempest\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , sculpted by\n       <a href="/wiki/Eric_Gill" title="Eric Gill">\n        Eric Gill\n       </a>\n       . Renovation of Broadcasting House began in 2002, and was completed in 2013.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Until it closed at the end of March 2013,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">\n        BBC Television\n       </a>\n       was based at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n        BBC Television Centre\n       </a>\n       , a purpose built television facility and the second built in the country located in\n       <a href="/wiki/White_City,_London" title="White City, London">\n        White City, London\n       </a>\n       . This facility has been host to a number of famous guests and programmes through the years, and its name and image is familiar with many British citizens. Nearby, the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_White_City" title="BBC White City">\n        BBC White City\n       </a>\n       complex contains numerous programme offices, housed in Centre House, the Media Centre and Broadcast Centre. It is in this area around\n       <a href="/wiki/Shepherd%27s_Bush" title="Shepherd\'s Bush">\n        Shepherd\'s Bush\n       </a>\n       that the majority of BBC employees work.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As part of a major reorganisation of BBC property, the entire BBC News operation relocated from the News Centre at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n        BBC Television Centre\n       </a>\n       to the refurbished Broadcasting House to create what is being described as "one of the world\'s largest live broadcast centres".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_(TV_channel)" title="BBC News (TV channel)">\n        BBC News Channel\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">\n        BBC World News\n       </a>\n       relocated to the premises in early 2013.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Broadcasting House is now also home to most of the BBC\'s national radio stations, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n        BBC World Service\n       </a>\n       . The major part of this plan involves the demolition of the two post-war extensions to the building and construction of an extension\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       designed by\n       <a href="/wiki/Richard_MacCormac" title="Richard MacCormac">\n        Sir Richard MacCormac\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/MJP_Architects" title="MJP Architects">\n        MJP Architects\n       </a>\n       . This move will concentrate the BBC\'s London operations, allowing them to sell\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Television_Centre" title="BBC Television Centre">\n        Television Centre\n       </a>\n       , which is expected to be completed by 2016.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_Article_-_TV_Centre_up_for_sale_94-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_Article_-_TV_Centre_up_for_sale-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to the scheme above, the BBC is in the process of making and producing more programmes outside London, involving production centres such as\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">\n        Belfast\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Cymru_Wales" title="BBC Cymru Wales">\n        Cardiff\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">\n        Glasgow\n       </a>\n       , Newcastle and, most notably, in\n       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">\n        Greater Manchester\n       </a>\n       as part of the "BBC North Project" scheme where several major departments, including\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_West" title="BBC North West">\n        BBC North West\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Manchester" title="BBC Manchester">\n        BBC Manchester\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">\n        BBC Sport\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">\n        BBC Children\'s\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">\n        CBeebies\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">\n        Radio 5 Live\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live_Sports_Extra" title="BBC Radio 5 Live Sports Extra">\n        BBC Radio 5 Live Sports Extra\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Breakfast" title="BBC Breakfast">\n         BBC Breakfast\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Learning" title="BBC Learning">\n        BBC Learning\n       </a>\n       and the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Philharmonic" title="BBC Philharmonic">\n        BBC Philharmonic\n       </a>\n       have all moved from their previous locations in either London or\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Broadcasting_House_(Manchester)" title="New Broadcasting House (Manchester)">\n        New Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       , Manchester to the new 200-acre (80ha)\n       <a href="/wiki/MediaCityUK" title="MediaCityUK">\n        MediaCityUK\n       </a>\n       production facilities in\n       <a href="/wiki/City_of_Salford" title="City of Salford">\n        Salford\n       </a>\n       , that form part of the large\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_North" title="BBC North">\n        BBC North Group\n       </a>\n       division and will therefore become the biggest staffing operation outside London.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_North_Website_96-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_North_Website-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As well as the two main sites in London (Broadcasting House and White City), there are seven other important BBC production centres in the UK, mainly specialising in different productions.\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House_(Cardiff)" title="Broadcasting House (Cardiff)">\n        Broadcasting House Cardiff\n       </a>\n       , has been home to\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Cymru_Wales" title="BBC Cymru Wales">\n        BBC Cymru Wales\n       </a>\n       , which specialises in drama production. Open since October 2011, and containing 7 new studios, Roath Lock\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">\n        <a href="#cite_note-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       is notable as the home of productions such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">\n         Doctor Who\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Casualty_(TV_series)" title="Casualty (TV series)">\n         Casualty\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       .\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House_(Belfast)" title="Broadcasting House (Belfast)">\n        Broadcasting House Belfast\n       </a>\n       , home to\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">\n        BBC Northern Ireland\n       </a>\n       , specialises in original drama and comedy, and has taken part in many co-productions with independent companies and notably with\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RT%C3%89" title="RT\xc3\x89">\n        RT\xc3\x89\n       </a>\n       in the Republic of Ireland.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">\n        BBC Scotland\n       </a>\n       , based in\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Pacific_Quay" title="BBC Pacific Quay">\n        Pacific Quay, Glasgow\n       </a>\n       is a large producer of programmes for the network, including several quiz shows. In England, the larger regions also produce some programming.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Previously, the largest hub of BBC programming from the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_English_Regions" title="BBC English Regions">\n        regions\n       </a>\n       is\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_North_West" title="BBC North West">\n        BBC North West\n       </a>\n       . At present they produce all Religious and Ethical programmes on the BBC, as well as other programmes such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/A_Question_of_Sport" title="A Question of Sport">\n         A Question of Sport\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . However, this is to be merged and expanded under the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_North" title="BBC North">\n        BBC North\n       </a>\n       project, which involved the region moving from\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Broadcasting_House_(Manchester)" title="New Broadcasting House (Manchester)">\n        New Broadcasting House\n       </a>\n       , Manchester, to\n       <a href="/wiki/MediaCityUK" title="MediaCityUK">\n        MediaCityUK\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_West_Midlands" title="BBC West Midlands">\n        BBC Midlands\n       </a>\n       , based at\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mailbox" title="The Mailbox">\n        The Mailbox\n       </a>\n       in Birmingham, also produces drama and contains the headquarters for the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_English_Regions" title="BBC English Regions">\n        English regions\n       </a>\n       and the BBC\'s daytime output. Other production centres include\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcasting_House_(Bristol)" title="Broadcasting House (Bristol)">\n        Broadcasting House Bristol\n       </a>\n       , home of\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_West" title="BBC West">\n        BBC West\n       </a>\n       and famously the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Natural_History_Unit" title="BBC Natural History Unit">\n        BBC Natural History Unit\n       </a>\n       and to a lesser extent,\n       <a href="/wiki/Quarry_Hill,_Leeds" title="Quarry Hill, Leeds">\n        Quarry Hill\n       </a>\n       in Leeds, home of\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Yorkshire" title="BBC Yorkshire">\n        BBC Yorkshire\n       </a>\n       . There are also many smaller local and regional studios throughout the UK, operating the BBC regional television services and the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Local_Radio" title="BBC Local Radio">\n        BBC Local Radio\n       </a>\n       stations.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC also operates several news gathering centres in various locations around the world, which provide news coverage of that region to the national and international news operations.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span id="Technology_(Atos_service)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Technology_.28Atos_service.29">\n        Technology (Atos service)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Technology (Atos service)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In 2004, the BBC contracted out its former BBC Technology division to the German engineering and electronics company\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siemens_IT_Solutions_and_Services" title="Siemens IT Solutions and Services">\n        Siemens IT Solutions and Services\n       </a>\n       (SIS),\n       <a href="/wiki/Outsourcing" title="Outsourcing">\n        outsourcing\n       </a>\n       its\n       <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">\n        IT\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Telephony" title="Telephony">\n        telephony\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_engineering" title="Broadcast engineering">\n        broadcast technology\n       </a>\n       systems.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc-2204_46-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-bbc-2204-46">\n         [46]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       When Atos Origin acquired the SIS division from\n       <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">\n        Siemens\n       </a>\n       in December 2010 for \xe2\x82\xac850 million (\xc2\xa3720m),\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cw-siemens_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cw-siemens-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       the BBC support contract also passed to\n       <a href="/wiki/Atos" title="Atos">\n        Atos\n       </a>\n       , and in July 2011, the BBC announced to staff that its technology support would become an Atos service.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atos-ariel_47-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-atos-ariel-47">\n         [47]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Siemens staff working on the BBC contract were transferred to Atos and BBC technology systems (including the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">\n        BBC website\n       </a>\n       ) are now managed by Atos. In 2011, the BBC\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Financial_Officer" title="Chief Financial Officer">\n        Chief Financial Officer\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Zarin_Patel" title="Zarin Patel">\n        Zarin Patel\n       </a>\n       stated to the\n       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">\n        House of Commons\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Public_Accounts_Committee_(United_Kingdom)" title="Public Accounts Committee (United Kingdom)">\n        Public Accounts Committee\n       </a>\n       that, following criticism of the BBC\'s management of major IT projects with Siemens (such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_Media_Initiative" title="Digital Media Initiative">\n        Digital Media Initiative\n       </a>\n       ), the BBC partnership with Atos would be instrumental in achieving cost savings of around \xc2\xa364 million as part of the BBC\'s "Delivering Quality First" programme.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publicaccounts_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-publicaccounts-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In 2012, the BBC\'s\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Technology_Officer" title="Chief Technology Officer">\n        Chief Technology Officer\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=John_Linwood_(BBC)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="John Linwood (BBC) (page does not exist)">\n        John Linwood\n       </a>\n       , expressed confidence in service improvements to the BBC\'s technology provision brought about by Atos. He also stated that supplier accountability had been strengthened following some high-profile technology failures which had taken place during the partnership with Siemens.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cw-linwood_100-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-cw-linwood-100">\n         [100]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Services">\n        Services\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Services">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="388" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/250px-BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/375px-BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_weekly_reach_2011-12.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Weekly reach of the BBC\'s domestic services from 2011 to 2012\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Trust_annual_report_11.2F12_101-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Trust_annual_report_11.2F12-101">\n           [101]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages_102-0">\n          <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages-102">\n           [102]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         Reach is the number of people who use the service at any point for more than 15 minutes in a week.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages_102-1">\n          <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages-102">\n           [102]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Television">\n        Television\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Television">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Television" title="BBC Television">\n        BBC Television\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC operates several television channels in the UK.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">\n        BBC One\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">\n        BBC Two\n       </a>\n       are the flagship television channels; others are\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Four" title="BBC Four">\n        BBC Four\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_(TV_channel)" title="BBC News (TV channel)">\n        BBC News\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Parliament" title="BBC Parliament">\n        BBC Parliament\n       </a>\n       , and two children\'s channels,\n       <a href="/wiki/CBBC_(TV_channel)" title="CBBC (TV channel)">\n        CBBC\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">\n        CBeebies\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">\n        Digital television\n       </a>\n       is now entrenched in the UK, with analogue transmission completely phased out as of December 2012.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n        <a href="#cite_note-103">\n         [103]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It also operates the\n       <a href="/wiki/Internet_television" title="Internet television">\n        internet television\n       </a>\n       service\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three_(online)" title="BBC Three (online)">\n        BBC Three\n       </a>\n       , which ceased broadcasting as a\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">\n        linear television channel\n       </a>\n       in February 2016.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tleft">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="718" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/300px-BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/450px-BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/600px-BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Television_weekly_reach_2011-12.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Weekly reach of the BBC\'s domestic television channels 2011\xe2\x80\x9312\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages_102-2">\n          <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages-102">\n           [102]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       BBC One is a regionalised TV service which provides opt-outs throughout the day for local news and other local programming. These variations are more pronounced in the BBC "Nations", i.e.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Northern_Ireland" title="BBC Northern Ireland">\n        Northern Ireland\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scotland" title="BBC Scotland">\n        Scotland\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Wales" title="BBC Wales">\n        Wales\n       </a>\n       , where the presentation is mostly carried out locally on BBC One and Two, and where programme schedules can vary greatly from that of the network. BBC Two variations exist in the Nations; however,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_English_Regions" title="BBC English Regions">\n        English regions\n       </a>\n       today rarely have the option to opt out as regional programming now only exists on BBC One. BBC Two was also the first channel to be transmitted on 625 lines in 1964, then carry a small-scale regular colour service from 1967. BBC One would follow in November 1969.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A new\n       <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">\n        Scottish Gaelic\n       </a>\n       television channel,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Alba_(TV_channel)" title="BBC Alba (TV channel)">\n        BBC Alba\n       </a>\n       , was launched in September 2008. It is also the first multi-genre channel to come entirely from Scotland with almost all of its programmes made in Scotland. The service was initially only available via\n       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_television" title="Satellite television">\n        satellite\n       </a>\n       but since June 2011 has been available to viewers in Scotland on\n       <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">\n        Freeview\n       </a>\n       and cable television.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n        <a href="#cite_note-104">\n         [104]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC currently operates\n       <a href="/wiki/High-definition_television" title="High-definition television">\n        HD\n       </a>\n       simulcasts of all its nationwide channels with the exception of\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Parliament" title="BBC Parliament">\n        BBC Parliament\n       </a>\n       . Until 26 March 2013, a separate channel called\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_HD" title="BBC HD">\n        BBC HD\n       </a>\n       was available, in place of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Two_HD" title="BBC Two HD">\n        BBC Two HD\n       </a>\n       . It launched on 9 June 2006, following a 12-month trial of the broadcasts. It became a proper channel in 2007, and screened HD programmes as simulcasts of the main network, or as repeats. The corporation has been producing programmes in the format for many years, and stated that it hoped to produce 100% of new programmes in HDTV by 2010.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">\n        <a href="#cite_note-105">\n         [105]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 3 November 2010, a high-definition simulcast of BBC One was launched, entitled\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_One_HD" title="BBC One HD">\n        BBC One HD\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Two_HD" title="BBC Two HD">\n        BBC Two HD\n       </a>\n       launched on 26 March 2013, replacing\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_HD" title="BBC HD">\n        BBC HD\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the Republic of Ireland, Belgium, the Netherlands and Switzerland, the BBC channels are available in a number of ways. In these countries digital and cable operators carry a range of BBC channels. These include BBC One, BBC Two and BBC World News, although viewers in the Republic of Ireland may receive BBC services via overspill from transmitters in Northern Ireland or Wales, or via "deflectors" \xe2\x80\x93 transmitters in the Republic which rebroadcast broadcasts from the UK,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n        <a href="#cite_note-106">\n         [106]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       received off-air, or from digital satellite.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since 1975, the BBC has also provided its TV programmes to the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">\n        British Forces Broadcasting Service (BFBS)\n       </a>\n       , allowing members of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Military of the United Kingdom">\n        UK military\n       </a>\n       serving abroad to watch them on four dedicated TV channels. From 27 March 2013, BFBS will carry versions of\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">\n        BBC One\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Two" title="BBC Two">\n        BBC Two\n       </a>\n       , which will include children\'s programming from\n       <a href="/wiki/CBBC" title="CBBC">\n        CBBC\n       </a>\n       , as well as carrying programming from\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three" title="BBC Three">\n        BBC Three\n       </a>\n       on a new channel called\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forces_TV" title="Forces TV">\n        BFBS Extra\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Since 2008, all the BBC channels are available to watch online through the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">\n        BBC iPlayer\n       </a>\n       service. This online streaming ability came about following experiments with live streaming, involving streaming certain channels in the UK.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n        <a href="#cite_note-107">\n         [107]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In February 2014, Director-General Tony Hall announced that the corporation needed to save \xc2\xa3100 million. In March 2014, the BBC confirmed plans for BBC Three to become an internet-only channel.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">\n        <a href="#cite_note-108">\n         [108]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Genome_Project">\n        Genome Project\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Genome Project">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Genome_Project" title="BBC Genome Project">\n        BBC Genome Project\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="590" data-file-width="1050" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Wikidata-logo.svg/40px-Wikidata-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Wikidata-logo.svg/60px-Wikidata-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Wikidata-logo.svg/80px-Wikidata-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/>\n        </td>\n        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikidata" title="Wikidata">\n          Wikidata\n         </a>\n         has the property:\n         <i>\n          <b>\n           <a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Property:P1573" title="d:Property:P1573">\n            Genome identifiers\n            <small>\n             (P1573)\n            </small>\n           </a>\n          </b>\n         </i>\n         (see\n         <a class="extiw" href="https://www.wikidata.org/wiki/Special:WhatLinksHere/Property:P1573" title="d:Special:WhatLinksHere/Property:P1573">\n          uses\n         </a>\n         )\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       In December 2012, the BBC completed a digitisation exercise, scanning the listings of all BBC programmes from an entire run of about 4,500 copies of the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Radio_Times" title="Radio Times">\n         Radio Times\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       magazine from the first, 1923, issue to 2009 (later listings already being held electronically), the "BBC Genome project", with a view to creating an online database of its programme output.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelion_109-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kelion-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       An earlier ten months of listings are to be obtained from other sources.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelion_109-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kelion-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       They identified around five million programmes, involving 8.5 million actors, presenters, writers and technical staff.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kelion_109-2">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Kelion-109">\n         [109]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Genome project was opened to public access on 15 October 2014, with corrections to OCR errors and changes to advertised schedules being\n       <a href="/wiki/Crowdsourcing" title="Crowdsourcing">\n        crowdsourced\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC-RTANL_110-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC-RTANL-110">\n         [110]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Radio">\n        Radio\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Radio">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="498" data-file-width="808" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/300px-BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/450px-BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png/600px-BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png 2x" width="300"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Radio_weekly_reach_2011-12.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Weekly reach of the BBC\'s national radio stations, both on analogue and digital.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages_102-3">\n          <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Annual_Report_2011-12_reach_pages-102">\n           [102]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">\n        BBC Radio\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Local_Radio" title="BBC Local Radio">\n        BBC Local Radio\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC has ten radio stations serving the whole of the UK, a further six stations in the "national regions" (\n       <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">\n        Wales\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">\n        Scotland\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">\n        Northern Ireland\n       </a>\n       ), and 40 other local stations serving defined areas of England. Of the ten national stations, five are major stations and are available on\n       <a href="/wiki/FM_broadcasting" title="FM broadcasting">\n        FM\n       </a>\n       and/or\n       <a href="/wiki/AM_broadcasting" title="AM broadcasting">\n        AM\n       </a>\n       as well as on\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_radio_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Digital radio in the United Kingdom">\n        DAB\n       </a>\n       and online. These are\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">\n        BBC Radio 1\n       </a>\n       , offering new music and popular styles and being notable for its chart show;\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_2" title="BBC Radio 2">\n        BBC Radio 2\n       </a>\n       , playing\n       <a href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary_music" title="Adult contemporary music">\n        Adult contemporary\n       </a>\n       , country and soul music amongst many other genres;\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_3" title="BBC Radio 3">\n        BBC Radio 3\n       </a>\n       , presenting classical and jazz music together with some spoken-word programming of a cultural nature in the evenings;\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4" title="BBC Radio 4">\n        BBC Radio 4\n       </a>\n       , focusing on current affairs, factual and other speech-based programming, including drama and comedy; and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">\n        BBC Radio 5 Live\n       </a>\n       , broadcasting 24-hour news, sport and talk programmes.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to these five stations, the BBC also runs a further five stations that broadcast on DAB and online only. These stations supplement and expand on the big five stations, and were launched in 2002.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1Xtra" title="BBC Radio 1Xtra">\n        BBC Radio 1Xtra\n       </a>\n       sisters Radio 1, and broadcasts new black music and urban tracks.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live_Sports_Extra" title="BBC Radio 5 Live Sports Extra">\n        BBC Radio 5 Live Sports Extra\n       </a>\n       sisters 5 Live and offers extra sport analysis, including broadcasting sports that previously were not covered.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_6_Music" title="BBC Radio 6 Music">\n        BBC Radio 6 Music\n       </a>\n       offers alternative music genres and is notable as a platform for new artists.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_7" title="BBC Radio 7">\n        BBC Radio 7\n       </a>\n       , later renamed\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_4_Extra" title="BBC Radio 4 Extra">\n        BBC Radio 4 Extra\n       </a>\n       , provided archive drama, comedy and children\'s programming. Following the change to Radio 4 Extra, the service has dropped a defined children\'s strand in favour of family-friendly drama and comedy. In addition, new programmes to complement Radio 4 programmes were introduced such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Ambridge_Extra" title="Ambridge Extra">\n         Ambridge Extra\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        Desert Island Discs revisited\n       </i>\n       . The final station is the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Asian_Network" title="BBC Asian Network">\n        BBC Asian Network\n       </a>\n       , providing music, talk and news to this section of the community. This station evolved out of Local radio stations serving certain areas, and as such this station is available on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medium_Wave" title="Medium Wave">\n        Medium Wave\n       </a>\n       frequency in some areas of the Midlands.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       As well as the national stations, the BBC also provides 40\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Local_Radio" title="BBC Local Radio">\n        BBC Local Radio\n       </a>\n       stations in England and the Channel Islands, each named for and covering a particular city and its surrounding area (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Bristol" title="BBC Radio Bristol">\n        BBC Radio Bristol\n       </a>\n       ), county or region (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Three_Counties_Radio" title="BBC Three Counties Radio">\n        BBC Three Counties Radio\n       </a>\n       ), or geographical area (e.g.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Solent" title="BBC Radio Solent">\n        BBC Radio Solent\n       </a>\n       covering the central south coast). A further six stations broadcast in what the BBC terms "the national regions": Wales, Scotland, and Northern Ireland. These are\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Wales" title="BBC Radio Wales">\n        BBC Radio Wales\n       </a>\n       (in English),\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Cymru" title="BBC Radio Cymru">\n        BBC Radio Cymru\n       </a>\n       (in\n       <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">\n        Welsh\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Scotland" title="BBC Radio Scotland">\n        BBC Radio Scotland\n       </a>\n       (in English),\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_nan_Gaidheal" title="BBC Radio nan Gaidheal">\n        BBC Radio nan Gaidheal\n       </a>\n       (in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" title="Scottish Gaelic language">\n        Scottish Gaelic\n       </a>\n       ),\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Ulster" title="BBC Radio Ulster">\n        BBC Radio Ulster\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Foyle" title="BBC Radio Foyle">\n        BBC Radio Foyle\n       </a>\n       , the latter being an opt-out station from Radio Ulster for the north-west of Northern Ireland.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC\'s UK national channels are also broadcast in the Channel Islands and the Isle of Man (although these\n       <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">\n        Crown dependencies\n       </a>\n       are outside the UK), and in the former there are two local stations \xe2\x80\x93\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Guernsey" title="BBC Guernsey">\n        BBC Guernsey\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_Jersey" title="BBC Radio Jersey">\n        BBC Radio Jersey\n       </a>\n       . There is no BBC local radio station, however, in the Isle of Man, partly because the island has long been served by the popular independent commercial station,\n       <a href="/wiki/Manx_Radio" title="Manx Radio">\n        Manx Radio\n       </a>\n       , which predates the existence of BBC Local Radio. BBC services in the dependencies are financed from\n       <a href="/wiki/Television_licence" title="Television licence">\n        television licence\n       </a>\n       fees which are set at the same level as those payable in the UK, although collected locally. This is the subject of some controversy in the Isle of Man since, as well as having no BBC Local Radio service, the island also lacks a local television news service analogous to that provided by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Channel_Islands_News" title="BBC Channel Islands News">\n        BBC Channel Islands\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">\n        <a href="#cite_note-111">\n         [111]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg/220px-BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg/330px-BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg/440px-BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_World_Questions_-_Hungary.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         BBC World Service \xe2\x80\x93 Jonathan Dimbleby broadcasting from Budapest\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       For a worldwide audience, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n        BBC World Service\n       </a>\n       provides news, current affairs and information in 28 languages, including English, around the world and is available in over 150 capital cities. It is broadcast worldwide on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shortwave" title="Shortwave">\n        shortwave\n       </a>\n       radio, DAB and online and has an estimated weekly audience of 192 million, and its websites have an audience of 38 million people per week.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n        <a href="#cite_note-112">\n         [112]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Since 2005, it is also available on DAB in the UK, a step not taken before, due to the way it is funded. The service is funded by a Parliamentary Grant-in-Aid, administered by the\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">\n        Foreign Office\n       </a>\n       ; however, following the Government\'s spending review in 2011, this funding will cease, and it will be funded for the first time through the Licence fee.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_World_Service_Annual_Review_2010_113-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBC_World_Service_Annual_Review_2010-113">\n         [113]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Service_Finance_details_114-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-World_Service_Finance_details-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In recent years, some services of the World Service have been reduced; the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">\n        Thai\n       </a>\n       service ended in 2006,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       as did the Eastern European languages, with resources diverted instead into the new\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Arabic_Television" title="BBC Arabic Television">\n        BBC Arabic Television\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Historically, the BBC was the only legal radio broadcaster based in the UK mainland until 1967, when\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/URY" title="URY">\n        University Radio York (URY)\n       </a>\n       , then under the name\n       <i>\n        Radio York\n       </i>\n       , was launched as the first, and now oldest, legal independent radio station in the country. However, the BBC did not enjoy a complete monopoly before this as several Continental stations, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Luxembourg_(English)" title="Radio Luxembourg (English)">\n        Radio Luxembourg\n       </a>\n       , had broadcast programmes in English to Britain since the 1930s and the Isle of Man-based\n       <a href="/wiki/Manx_Radio" title="Manx Radio">\n        Manx Radio\n       </a>\n       began in 1964. Today, despite the advent of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commercial_radio" title="Commercial radio">\n        commercial radio\n       </a>\n       , BBC radio stations remain among the most listened to in the country, with Radio 2 having the largest audience share (up to 16.8% in 2011\xe2\x80\x9312) and Radios 1 and 4 ranked second and third in terms of weekly\n       <a href="/wiki/Reach_(advertising)" title="Reach (advertising)">\n        reach\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       BBC programming is also available to other services and in other countries. Since 1943, the BBC has provided radio programming to the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Forces_Broadcasting_Service" title="British Forces Broadcasting Service">\n        British Forces Broadcasting Service\n       </a>\n       , which broadcasts in countries where British troops are stationed.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">\n        BBC Radio 1\n       </a>\n       is also carried in the United States and\n       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n        Canada\n       </a>\n       on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirius_XM_Radio" title="Sirius XM Radio">\n        Sirius XM Radio\n       </a>\n       (online streaming only).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC is a patron of The\n       <a href="/wiki/Radio_Academy" title="Radio Academy">\n        Radio Academy\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="News">\n        News\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: News">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="1880" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg/170px-BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg/255px-BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg/340px-BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Television_Centre_Newsroom_KristynaM_Flickr.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The former BBC Newsroom in London\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">\n        BBC News\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       BBC News is the largest broadcast news gathering operation in the world,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-About_BBC_News_Website_119-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-About_BBC_News_Website-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       providing services to BBC domestic radio as well as television networks such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_(TV_channel)" title="BBC News (TV channel)">\n        BBC News\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Parliament" title="BBC Parliament">\n        BBC Parliament\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">\n        BBC World News\n       </a>\n       . In addition to this, news stories are available on the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Red_Button" title="BBC Red Button">\n        BBC Red Button\n       </a>\n       service and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_Online" title="BBC News Online">\n        BBC News Online\n       </a>\n       .
