In addition to this, the BBC has been developing new ways to access BBC News, as a result has launched the service on BBC Mobile, making it accessible to mobile phones and PDAs, as well as developing alerts by e-mail, digital television, and on computers through a\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Alerts" title="BBC Alerts">\n        desktop alert\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Ratings figures suggest that during major incidents such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/7_July_2005_London_bombings" title="7 July 2005 London bombings">\n        7 July 2005 London bombings\n       </a>\n       or royal events, the UK audience overwhelmingly turns to the BBC\'s coverage as opposed to its commercial rivals.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 7 July 2005, the day that there were a series of coordinated bomb blasts on London\'s public transport system, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">\n        BBC Online\n       </a>\n       website recorded an all time\n       <a href="/wiki/Bandwidth_(computing)" title="Bandwidth (computing)">\n        bandwidth\n       </a>\n       peak of 11\n       <a href="/wiki/Gigabit" title="Gigabit">\n        Gb\n       </a>\n       /s at 12.00 on 7 July. BBC News received some 1\xc2\xa0billion total hits on the day of the event (including all images, text and\n       <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">\n        HTML\n       </a>\n       ), serving some 5.5\n       <a href="/wiki/Terabyte" title="Terabyte">\n        terabytes\n       </a>\n       of data. At peak times during the day there were 40,000 page requests per second for the BBC News website. The previous day\'s announcement of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2012_Olympics" title="2012 Olympics">\n        2012 Olympics\n       </a>\n       being awarded to London caused a peak of around 5\xc2\xa0Gbit/s. The previous all-time high at\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">\n        BBC Online\n       </a>\n       was caused by the announcement of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">\n        Michael Jackson\n       </a>\n       verdict, which used 7.2\xc2\xa0Gbit/s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Internet">\n        Internet\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Internet">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Online" title="BBC Online">\n        BBC Online\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC\'s online presence includes a comprehensive\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_Online" title="BBC News Online">\n        news website\n       </a>\n       and archive. It was launched as BBC Online, before being renamed BBCi, then bbc.co.uk, before it was rebranded back as BBC Online. The website is funded by the Licence fee, but uses\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geo_targeting" title="Geo targeting">\n        GeoIP\n       </a>\n       technology, allowing advertisements to be carried on the site when viewed outside of the UK.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The BBC claims the site to be "Europe\'s most popular content-based site"\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and states that 13.2\xc2\xa0million people in the UK visit the site\'s more than two million pages each day.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">\n        <a href="#cite_note-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       According to\n       <a href="/wiki/Alexa_Internet" title="Alexa Internet">\n        Alexa\'s\n       </a>\n       TrafficRank system, in July 2008 BBC Online was the 27th most popular English Language website in the world,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and the 46th most popular overall.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The centre of the website is the Homepage, which features a modular layout. Users can choose which modules, and which information, is displayed on their homepage, allowing the user to customise it. This system was first launched in December 2007, becoming permanent in February 2008, and has undergone a few aesthetical changes since then.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The Homepage then has links to other micro-sites, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_News_Online" title="BBC News Online">\n        BBC News Online\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">\n        Sport\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Weather" title="BBC Weather">\n        Weather\n       </a>\n       , TV and Radio. As part of the site, every programme on BBC Television or Radio is given its own page, with bigger programmes getting their own micro-site, and as a result it is often common for viewers and listeners to be told\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uniform_Resource_Locator" title="Uniform Resource Locator">\n        website addresses\n       </a>\n       (URLs) for the programme website.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Another large part of the site also allows users to watch and listen to most Television and Radio output live and for seven days after broadcast using the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_iPlayer" title="BBC iPlayer">\n        BBC iPlayer\n       </a>\n       platform, which launched on 27 July 2007, and initially used\n       <a href="/wiki/Peer-to-peer" title="Peer-to-peer">\n        peer-to-peer\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">\n        DRM\n       </a>\n       technology to deliver both radio and TV content of the last seven days for offline use for up to 30\xc2\xa0days, since then video is now streamed directly. Also, through participation in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Creative_Archive_Licence" title="Creative Archive Licence">\n        Creative Archive Licence\n       </a>\n       group, bbc.co.uk allowed legal downloads of selected archive material via the internet.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC has often included learning as part of its online service, running services such as\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Jam" title="BBC Jam">\n        BBC Jam\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Learning_Zone" title="BBC Learning Zone">\n        Learning Zone Class Clips\n       </a>\n       and also runs services such as\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_WebWise" title="BBC WebWise">\n        BBC WebWise\n       </a>\n       and First Click which are designed to teach people how to use the internet.\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Jam" title="BBC Jam">\n        BBC Jam\n       </a>\n       was a free online service, delivered through broadband and narrowband connections, providing high-quality interactive resources designed to stimulate learning at home and at school. Initial content was made available in January 2006; however, BBC Jam was suspended on 20 March 2007 due to allegations made to the\n       <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">\n        European Commission\n       </a>\n       that it was damaging the interests of the commercial sector of the industry.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">\n        <a href="#cite_note-129">\n         [129]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In recent years, some major on-line companies and politicians have complained that BBC Online receives too much funding from the television licence, meaning that other websites are unable to compete with the vast amount of advertising-free on-line content available on BBC Online.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">\n        <a href="#cite_note-130">\n         [130]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Some have proposed that the amount of licence fee money spent on BBC Online should be reduced\xe2\x80\x94either being replaced with funding from advertisements or subscriptions, or a reduction in the amount of content available on the site.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">\n        <a href="#cite_note-131">\n         [131]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In response to this the BBC carried out an investigation, and has now set in motion a plan to change the way it provides its online services. BBC Online will now attempt to fill in gaps in the market, and will guide users to other websites for currently existing market provision. (For example, instead of providing local events information and timetables, users will be guided to outside websites already providing that information.) Part of this plan included the BBC closing some of its websites, and rediverting money to redevelop other parts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">\n        <a href="#cite_note-132">\n         [132]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">\n        <a href="#cite_note-133">\n         [133]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       On 26 February 2010,\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">\n        The Times\n       </a>\n       claimed that\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mark_Thompson_(television_executive)" title="Mark Thompson (television executive)">\n        Mark Thompson\n       </a>\n       , Director General of the BBC, proposed that the BBC\'s web output should be cut by 50%, with online staff numbers and budgets reduced by 25% in a bid to scale back BBC operations and allow commercial rivals more room.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">\n        <a href="#cite_note-134">\n         [134]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       On 2 March 2010, the BBC reported that it will cut its website spending by 25% and close BBC 6 Music and Asian Network, as part of Mark Thompson\'s plans to make "a smaller, fitter BBC for the digital age".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">\n        <a href="#cite_note-135">\n         [135]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">\n        <a href="#cite_note-136">\n         [136]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Interactive_television">\n        Interactive television\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Interactive television">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Red_Button" title="BBC Red Button">\n        BBC Red Button\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       BBC Red Button is the brand name for the BBC\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Interactive_television" title="Interactive television">\n        interactive\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Digital_television" title="Digital television">\n        digital television\n       </a>\n       services, which are available through\n       <a href="/wiki/Freeview_(UK)" title="Freeview (UK)">\n        Freeview\n       </a>\n       (digital terrestrial), as well as\n       <a href="/wiki/Freesat" title="Freesat">\n        Freesat\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sky_(UK_%26_Ireland)" title="Sky (UK &amp; Ireland)">\n        Sky\n       </a>\n       (satellite), and\n       <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Media" title="Virgin Media">\n        Virgin Media\n       </a>\n       (cable). Unlike\n       <a href="/wiki/Ceefax" title="Ceefax">\n        Ceefax\n       </a>\n       , the service\'s analogue counterpart, BBC Red Button is able to display full-colour graphics, photographs, and video, as well as programmes and can be accessed from any BBC channel. The service carries News, Weather and Sport 24 hours a day, but also provides extra features related to programmes specific at that time. Examples include viewers to play along at home to gameshows, to give, voice and vote on opinions to issues, as used alongside programmes such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Question_Time_(TV_series)" title="Question Time (TV series)">\n         Question Time\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . At some points in the year, when multiple sporting events occur, some coverage of less mainstream sports or games are frequently placed on the Red Button for viewers to watch. Frequently, other features are added unrelated to programmes being broadcast at that time, such as the broadcast of the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">\n         Doctor Who\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       animated episode\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Dreamland_(Doctor_Who)" title="Dreamland (Doctor Who)">\n         Dreamland\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in November 2009.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">\n        Music\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Music">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2832" data-file-width="4256" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg/220px-BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg/330px-BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg/440px-BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BBC_Big_Band_-_Town_Hall_Birmingham_-_May_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         The\n         <a href="/wiki/BBC_Big_Band" title="BBC Big Band">\n          BBC Big Band\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC employs staff orchestras, a choir, and supports two amateur choruses, based in BBC venues across the UK; the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Symphony_Orchestra" title="BBC Symphony Orchestra">\n        BBC Symphony Orchestra\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Singers" title="BBC Singers">\n        BBC Singers\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Symphony_Chorus" title="BBC Symphony Chorus">\n        BBC Symphony Chorus\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Big_Band" title="BBC Big Band">\n        BBC Big Band\n       </a>\n       based in London, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Scottish_Symphony_Orchestra" title="BBC Scottish Symphony Orchestra">\n        BBC Scottish Symphony Orchestra\n       </a>\n       in Glasgow, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Philharmonic" title="BBC Philharmonic">\n        BBC Philharmonic\n       </a>\n       in Manchester, the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Concert_Orchestra" title="BBC Concert Orchestra">\n        BBC Concert Orchestra\n       </a>\n       based in Watford and the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_National_Orchestra_of_Wales" title="BBC National Orchestra of Wales">\n        BBC National Orchestra of Wales\n       </a>\n       in Cardiff. It also buys a selected number of broadcasts from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ulster_Orchestra" title="Ulster Orchestra">\n        Ulster Orchestra\n       </a>\n       in Belfast. Many famous musicians of every genre have played at the BBC, such as\n       <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">\n        The Beatles\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        The Beatles Live at the BBC\n       </i>\n       is one of their many albums). The BBC is also responsible for the United Kingdom coverage of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">\n        Eurovision Song Contest\n       </a>\n       , a show with which the broadcaster has been associated for over 50 years. The BBC also operates the division of BBC Audiobooks sometimes found in association with Chivers Audiobooks.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other">\n        Other\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Other">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The BBC operates other ventures in addition to their broadcasting arm. In addition to broadcasting output on television and radio, some programmes are also displayed on the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Big_Screen" title="BBC Big Screen">\n        BBC Big Screens\n       </a>\n       located in several central-city locations. The BBC and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_and_Commonwealth_Office" title="Foreign and Commonwealth Office">\n        Foreign and Commonwealth Office\n       </a>\n       also jointly run\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Monitoring" title="BBC Monitoring">\n        BBC Monitoring\n       </a>\n       , which monitors radio, television, the press and the internet worldwide. The BBC also developed several computers throughout the 1980s, most notably the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Micro" title="BBC Micro">\n        BBC Micro\n       </a>\n       , which ran alongside the corporation\'s educational aims and programming.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In 1951, in conjunction with\n       <a href="/wiki/Oxford_University_Press" title="Oxford University Press">\n        Oxford University Press\n       </a>\n       the BBC published\n       <i>\n        The BBC Hymn Book\n       </i>\n       which was intended to be used by radio listeners to follow hymns being broadcast. The book was published both with and without music, the music edition being entitled\n       <i>\n        The BBC Hymn Book with Music\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">\n        <a href="#cite_note-137">\n         [137]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The book contained 542 popular hymns.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ceefax">\n        Ceefax\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Ceefax">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Ceefax" title="Ceefax">\n        Ceefax\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC provided the world\'s first teletext service called\n       <a href="/wiki/Ceefax" title="Ceefax">\n        Ceefax\n       </a>\n       (near-homonymous with "See Facts") on 23 September 1974 until 23 October 2012 on the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_1" title="BBC 1">\n        BBC 1\n       </a>\n       analogue channel then later on\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_2" title="BBC 2">\n        BBC 2\n       </a>\n       . It showed informational pages such as News, Sport and the Weather. on New Year\'s Eve in 1974, competition from\n       <a href="/wiki/ITV_plc" title="ITV plc">\n        ITV\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/ORACLE_(teletext)" title="ORACLE (teletext)">\n        Oracle\n       </a>\n       tried to compete with Ceefax. Oracle closed on New Year\'s Eve, 1992. During its lifetime it attracted millions of viewers, right up to 2012, prior to the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UK_digital_transition" title="UK digital transition">\n        digital switchover in the United Kingdom\n       </a>\n       . It ceased transmission at 23:32:19 BST on 23 October 2012 after 38 years. Since then, the BBC\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Red_Button" title="BBC Red Button">\n        Red Button Service\n       </a>\n       has provided a digital-like information system that replaced Ceefax.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Upcoming_online_video_streaming_service">\n        Upcoming online video streaming service\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Upcoming online video streaming service">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The BBC have announced a new upcoming online video streaming service, currently known by the name Britflix.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">\n        <a href="#cite_note-138">\n         [138]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">\n        <a href="#cite_note-139">\n         [139]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_activities">\n        Commercial activities\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Commercial activities">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Worldwide" title="BBC Worldwide">\n        BBC Worldwide\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       BBC Worldwide Limited is the wholly owned commercial subsidiary of the BBC, responsible for the commercial exploitation of BBC programmes and other properties, including a number of television stations throughout the world. It was formed following the restructuring of its predecessor, BBC Enterprises, in 1995.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The company owns and administers a number of commercial stations around the world operating in a number of territories and on a number of different platforms. The channel\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Entertainment" title="BBC Entertainment">\n        BBC Entertainment\n       </a>\n       shows current and archive entertainment programming to viewers in Europe, Africa, Asia and the Middle East, with the BBC Worldwide channels\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_America" title="BBC America">\n        BBC America\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Canada" title="BBC Canada">\n        BBC Canada\n       </a>\n       (Joint venture with\n       <a href="/wiki/Corus_Entertainment" title="Corus Entertainment">\n        Corus Entertainment\n       </a>\n       ) showing similar programming in the North America region and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_UKTV" title="BBC UKTV">\n        BBC UKTV\n       </a>\n       in the Australasia region. The company also airs two channels aimed at children, an international\n       <a href="/wiki/CBeebies" title="CBeebies">\n        CBeebies\n       </a>\n       channel and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Kids" title="BBC Kids">\n        BBC Kids\n       </a>\n       , a joint venture with\n       <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_Network" title="Knowledge Network">\n        Knowledge Network Corporation\n       </a>\n       , which airs programmes under the CBeebies and BBC K brands. The company also runs the channels\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Knowledge_(international)" title="BBC Knowledge (international)">\n        BBC Knowledge\n       </a>\n       , broadcasting factual and learning programmes, and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Lifestyle" title="BBC Lifestyle">\n        BBC Lifestyle\n       </a>\n       , broadcasting programmes based on themes of Food, Style and Wellbeing. In addition to this, BBC Worldwide runs an international version of the channel\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_HD_Scandinavia" title="BBC HD Scandinavia">\n        BBC HD\n       </a>\n       , and provides HD simulcasts of the channels BBC Knowledge and BBC America.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       BBC Worldwide also distributes the 24-hour international news channel\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">\n        BBC World News\n       </a>\n       . The station is separate from BBC Worldwide to maintain the station\'s neutral point of view, but is distributed by BBC Worldwide. The channel itself is the oldest surviving entity of its kind, and has 50 foreign news bureaus and correspondents in nearly all countries in the world.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_140-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       As officially surveyed it is available to more than 294\xc2\xa0million households, significantly more than\n       <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">\n        CNN\n       </a>\n       \'s estimated 200\xc2\xa0million.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_140-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-140">\n         [140]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In addition to these international channels, BBC Worldwide also owns, together with\n       <a href="/wiki/Scripps_Networks_Interactive" title="Scripps Networks Interactive">\n        Scripps Networks Interactive\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/UKTV" title="UKTV">\n        UKTV\n       </a>\n       network of ten channels. These channels contain BBC archive programming to be rebroadcast on their respective channels:\n       <a href="/wiki/Alibi_(TV_channel)" title="Alibi (TV channel)">\n        Alibi\n       </a>\n       , crime dramas;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drama_(TV_channel)" title="Drama (TV channel)">\n        Drama\n       </a>\n       , drama, launched in 2013;\n       <a href="/wiki/Dave_(TV_channel)" title="Dave (TV channel)">\n        Dave\n       </a>\n       (slogan: "The Home of Witty Banter");\n       <a href="/wiki/Eden_(TV_channel)" title="Eden (TV channel)">\n        Eden\n       </a>\n       , nature;\n       <a href="/wiki/Gold_(UK_TV_channel)" title="Gold (UK TV channel)">\n        Gold\n       </a>\n       , comedy;\n       <a href="/wiki/Good_Food" title="Good Food">\n        Good Food\n       </a>\n       , cookery;\n       <a href="/wiki/Home_(TV_channel)" title="Home (TV channel)">\n        Home\n       </a>\n       , home and garden;\n       <a href="/wiki/Really_(TV_channel)" title="Really (TV channel)">\n        Really\n       </a>\n       , female programming;\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Watch_(TV_channel)" title="Watch (TV channel)">\n        Watch\n       </a>\n       , entertainment; and\n       <a href="/wiki/Yesterday_(TV_channel)" title="Yesterday (TV channel)">\n        Yesterday\n       </a>\n       , history programming.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to these channels, many BBC programmes are sold via BBC Worldwide to foreign television stations with comedy, documentaries and\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Costume_drama" title="Costume drama">\n        historical drama\n       </a>\n       productions being the most popular. In addition, BBC television news appears nightly on many\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service">\n        Public Broadcasting Service\n       </a>\n       stations in the United States, as do reruns of BBC programmes such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/EastEnders" title="EastEnders">\n         EastEnders\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and in New Zealand on\n       <a href="/wiki/TVNZ_1" title="TVNZ 1">\n        TVNZ 1\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to programming, BBC Worldwide produces material to accompany programmes. The company maintained the publishing arm of the BBC,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_Magazines" title="BBC Magazines">\n        BBC Magazines\n       </a>\n       , which published the\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Radio_Times" title="Radio Times">\n         Radio Times\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       as well as a number of magazines that support BBC programming such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Top_Gear_(magazine)" title="Top Gear (magazine)">\n         BBC Top Gear\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Good_Food" title="BBC Good Food">\n         BBC Good Food\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Sky_at_Night" title="The Sky at Night">\n         BBC Sky at Night\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBC_History_(magazine)" title="BBC History (magazine)">\n         BBC History\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Wildlife" title="BBC Wildlife">\n         BBC Wildlife\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/BBC_Music_Magazine" title="BBC Music Magazine">\n         BBC Music\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . BBC Magazines was sold to Exponent Private Equity in 2011, which merged it with Origin Publishing (previously owned by BBC Worldwide between 2004 and 2006) to form\n       <a href="/wiki/Immediate_Media_Company" title="Immediate Media Company">\n        Immediate Media Company\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       BBC Worldwide also publishes books, to accompany programmes such as\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">\n         Doctor Who\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       under the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Books" title="BBC Books">\n        BBC Books\n       </a>\n       brand, a publishing imprint majority owned by\n       <a href="/wiki/Random_House" title="Random House">\n        Random House\n       </a>\n       . Soundtrack albums, talking books and sections of radio broadcasts are also sold under the brand\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Records" title="BBC Records">\n        BBC Records\n       </a>\n       , with DVDs also being sold and licensed in large quantities to consumers both in the UK and abroad under the\n       <a href="/wiki/2_Entertain" title="2 Entertain">\n        2 Entertain\n       </a>\n       brand. Archive programming and classical music recordings are sold under the brand BBC Legends.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_significance">\n        Cultural significance\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cultural significance">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Until the development, popularisation, and domination of television, radio was the broadcast medium upon which people in the United Kingdom relied. It "reached into every home in the land, and simultaneously united the nation, an important factor during the Second World War".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry_141-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Perry-141">\n         [141]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The BBC introduced the world\'s first "high-definition"\n       <a href="/wiki/405-line_television_system" title="405-line television system">\n        405-line television\n       </a>\n       service in 1936. It suspended its television service during the Second World War and until 1946, but remained the only television broadcaster in the UK until 1955, when Independent Television (\n       <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">\n        ITV\n       </a>\n       ) began operating.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry16_142-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Perry16-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       This heralded the transformation of television into a popular and dominant medium. Nevertheless, "throughout the 1950s radio still remained the dominant source of broadcast comedy".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry16_142-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Perry16-142">\n         [142]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Further, the BBC was the only legal radio broadcaster until 1968 (when\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/URY" title="URY">\n        URY\n       </a>\n       obtained their first licence).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">\n        <a href="#cite_note-143">\n         [143]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Despite the advent of commercial television and radio, the BBC has remained one of the main elements in\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_popular_culture" title="British popular culture">\n        British popular culture\n       </a>\n       through its obligation to produce TV and radio programmes for mass audiences.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Public_service_144-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Public_service-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">\n        <a href="#cite_note-145">\n         [145]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the arrival of BBC2 allowed the BBC also to make programmes for minority interests in drama, documentaries, current affairs, entertainment, and sport. Examples cited include the television series\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Civilisation_(TV_series)" title="Civilisation (TV series)">\n         Civilisation\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">\n         Doctor Who\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/I,_Claudius_(TV_series)" title="I, Claudius (TV series)">\n         I, Claudius\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Monty_Python%27s_Flying_Circus" title="Monty Python\'s Flying Circus">\n         Monty Python\'s Flying Circus\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Pot_Black" title="Pot Black">\n         Pot Black\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , and\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Tonight_(1957_TV_series)" title="Tonight (1957 TV series)">\n         Tonight\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , but other examples can be given in each of these fields as shown by the BBC\'s entries in the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">\n        British Film Institute\n       </a>\n       \'s 2000 list of the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/100_Greatest_British_Television_Programmes" title="100 Greatest British Television Programmes">\n        100 Greatest British Television Programmes\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tv100_146-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-tv100-146">\n         [146]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The export of BBC programmes both through services like the\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">\n        BBC World Service\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_News" title="BBC World News">\n        BBC World News\n       </a>\n       , as well as through the channels operated by\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_Worldwide" title="BBC Worldwide">\n        BBC Worldwide\n       </a>\n       , means that audiences can consume BBC productions worldwide.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The term "BBC English" was used as an alternative name for\n       <a href="/wiki/Received_Pronunciation" title="Received Pronunciation">\n        Received Pronunciation\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <i>\n        English Pronouncing Dictionary\n       </i>\n       uses the term "BBC Pronunciation" to label its recommendations.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">\n        <a href="#cite_note-147">\n         [147]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However, the BBC itself now makes more use of\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_accents_of_English_speakers" title="Regional accents of English speakers">\n        regional accents\n       </a>\n       in order to reflect the diversity of the UK, while continuing to expect clarity and fluency of its presenters.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-accents_148-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-accents-148">\n         [148]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       From its "starchy" beginnings, the BBC has also become more inclusive, and now attempts to accommodate the interests of all strata of society and all minorities, because they all pay the licence fee.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diversityPolicy_149-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-diversityPolicy-149">\n         [149]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Competition from\n       <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">\n        Independent Television\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Channel_4" title="Channel 4">\n        Channel 4\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Sky_Broadcasting" title="British Sky Broadcasting">\n        Sky\n       </a>\n       , and other broadcast-television stations has lessened the BBC\'s influence, but its public broadcasting remains a major influence on British popular culture.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Public_service_144-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Public_service-144">\n         [144]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Attitudes_toward_the_BBC_in_popular_culture">\n        Attitudes toward the BBC in popular culture\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Attitudes toward the BBC in popular culture">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Older domestic UK audiences often refer to the BBC as "the Beeb", a nickname originally coined by\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sellers" title="Peter Sellers">\n        Peter Sellers\n       </a>\n       on\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Goon_Show" title="The Goon Show">\n         The Goon Show\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       in the 1950s, when he referred to the "Beeb Beeb Ceeb". It was then borrowed, shortened and popularised by\n       <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Everett" title="Kenny Everett">\n        Kenny Everett\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">\n        <a href="#cite_note-150">\n         [150]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Another nickname, now less commonly used, is "Auntie", said to originate from the old-fashioned "Auntie knows best" attitude, or the idea of aunties and uncles who are present in the background of one\'s life (but possibly a reference to the "aunties" and "uncles" who presented children\'s programmes in the early days)\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151">\n        <a href="#cite_note-151">\n         [151]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       in the days when\n       <a href="/wiki/John_Reith,_1st_Baron_Reith" title="John Reith, 1st Baron Reith">\n        John Reith\n       </a>\n       , the BBC\'s first director general, was in charge. The two nicknames have also been used together as "Auntie Beeb".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152">\n        <a href="#cite_note-152">\n         [152]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism_and_controversies">\n        Criticism and controversies\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Criticism and controversies">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main articles:\n       <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_BBC" title="Criticism of the BBC">\n        Criticism of the BBC\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/BBC_controversies" title="BBC controversies">\n        BBC controversies\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The BBC has faced various accusations regarding many topics: the Iraq war, politics, ethics and religion, as well as funding and staffing. It also has been involved in numerous controversies because of its different, sometimes controversial coverage of specific news stories and programming. In October 2014, the BBC Trust issued the "BBC complaints framework",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCComplaintsFW_153-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-BBCComplaintsFW-153">\n         [153]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       outlining complaints and appeals procedures. However, the regulatory oversight of the BBC may be transferred to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OFCOM" title="OFCOM">\n        OFCOM\n       </a>\n       . The British "\n       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">\n        House of Commons\n       </a>\n       Select Committee on Culture Media and Sport" recommended in its report "The Future of the BBC",\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154">\n        <a href="#cite_note-154">\n         [154]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       that OFCOM should become the final arbiter of complaints made about the BBC.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TrustToOfcom_155-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-TrustToOfcom-155">\n         [155]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Accusations of a bias against the government and the Conservative Party were often made against the Corporation by members of\n       <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">\n        Margaret Thatcher\n       </a>\n       \'s 1980s Conservative government. BBC has long faced accusations of liberal and leftwing bias,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156">\n        <a href="#cite_note-156">\n         [156]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       presenter\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Marr" title="Andrew Marr">\n        Andrew Marr\n       </a>\n       has said that "The BBC is not impartial or neutral. It has a liberal bias, not so much a party-political bias. It is better expressed as a cultural liberal bias", while former BBC director Roger Mosey classified it as "liberal defensive."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157">\n        <a href="#cite_note-157">\n         [157]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158">\n        <a href="#cite_note-158">\n         [158]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159">\n        <a href="#cite_note-159">\n         [159]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Conversely, the BBC has been criticised by\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">\n         The Guardian\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       columnist,\n       <a href="/wiki/Owen_Jones_(writer)" title="Owen Jones (writer)">\n        Owen Jones\n       </a>\n       , who has said that "the truth is the BBC is stacked full of rightwingers."\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160">\n        <a href="#cite_note-160">\n         [160]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <a href="/wiki/Paul_Mason_(journalist)" title="Paul Mason (journalist)">\n        Paul Mason\n       </a>\n       , the former Economics Editor of the BBC\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Newsnight" title="Newsnight">\n        Newsnight\n       </a>\n       programme, has also criticised the BBC as "unionist" in relation to the BBC\'s coverage of the 2014 Scottish referendum campaign and "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neo-liberal" title="Neo-liberal">\n        neo-liberal\n       </a>\n       ".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161">\n        <a href="#cite_note-161">\n         [161]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However,\n       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Sissons" title="Peter Sissons">\n        Peter Sissons\n       </a>\n       , a main news presenter at the BBC from 1989\xe2\x80\x942009, who from 1964\xe2\x80\x941989 worked as a journalist and then senior presenter at\n       <a href="/wiki/ITN" title="ITN">\n        ITN\n       </a>\n       , latterly at\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Channel_4_News" title="Channel 4 News">\n         Channel 4 News\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       , says "At the core of the BBC, in its very DNA, is a way of thinking that is firmly of the Left".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162">\n        <a href="#cite_note-162">\n         [162]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The BBC has also been characterised as a pro-\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monarchist" title="Monarchist">\n        monarchist\n       </a>\n       institution.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163">\n        <a href="#cite_note-163">\n         [163]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The BBC was also accused of propaganda by journalist and author\n       <a href="/wiki/Toby_Young" title="Toby Young">\n        Toby Young\n       </a>\n       , due to what he believed to be an anti-Brexit approach including a whole day of live programming on migration.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164">\n        <a href="#cite_note-164">\n         [164]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The BBC World Service was involved in the Kyrgyz revolution in April 2010. One of the news presenters and a producer of the BBC World Service language, was revealed to have participated in the opposition movement at the time, with the goal to overthrow the Kyrgyzstan government led by president\n       <a href="/wiki/Kurmanbek_Bakiyev" title="Kurmanbek Bakiyev">\n        Kurmanbek Bakiyev\n       </a>\n       using BBC resources. The BBC producer resigned from his post in 2010 once the news of his participation in the revolution became public. The BBC World Service neither confirmed nor denied this story, nor did the service issue a statement about this story.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165">\n        <a href="#cite_note-165">\n         [165]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">\n        Awards and nominations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=BBC&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">\n       <tr>\n        <td class="mbox-image">\n         <a class="image" text-align: center;">\n         Nominated\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Logos_and_symbols_of_the_BBC">\n        Logos and symbols of BBC World Service.\n           <q>\n            The BBC, including World Service, operates under two constitutional documents \xe2\x80\x93 its Royal Charter and the Licence and Agreement. The Charter gives the Corporation legal existence, sets out its objectives and constitution, and also deals with such matters as advisory bodies. Under the Royal Charter, the BBC must obtain a licence from the Home Secretary. The License, which is coupled with an Agreement between the Minister and the Corporation, lays down the terms and conditions under which the BBC is allowed to broadcast.\n           </q>\n
